Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called it "cure contuse," which is that you make behind the patient who has this illness to remove the hair on his forehead, then you make III incisions on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as far as II doigths in the middle of the forehead going downwards until the nose, and the other two at each side above the temples, and beware of cutting the arteries that are at both sides above the temples; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the II mandibles, and let each wound be the size of III doigths across; and prepare a piece of sponge and much cloth for wiping the blood, then put the spatumile sharp on both sides where this is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is next to the temple until the second incision; and scrape all the skin that is between the II incisions to the surface which is on top of the bone, then do the same from the middle incision until the other second one, and then withdraw this spatumile.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Insert into the first groove the instrument which is called "cultellaire", and it is very well cutting on one side, and on the other side it is smooth, not cutting, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge towards the flesh of the heart, and the smooth side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle groove.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes so that the incision is continuous until it reaches near the heart, and then make another incision in the middle groove to the other side; and then draw out blood evenly, and press the area for the blood to be taken; then place a piece of old cotton in each groove, and put on cloths moistened with wine, oil, and honey, and guard against abscesses from occurring; and on the third day loosen the bandage, and bring generous poultices of vinegar water, then treat it with ointment basilicon with rose oil, and other treatments used for wounds until he is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the rheum of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a catarrh comes suddenly to someone, and you see the eyes swollen and small, and the sight weakened, and the membranes burned; and the hair falls out, and there is pain in the head with severe shivering, and the patient sneezes; then you know by these symptoms that those matters and that catarrh do not come from any single vein, but from many veins, and the phlegm that causes it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient to lie with their back against their forehead, then make a large incision across the forehead, and another one from the middle of the head.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And start from the incision on the left temple to the right temple, and make the cut until you reach the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves in the temples that move when chewing; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate between the two edges of the incision and place old cotton there, and cover with linen bandages; then bind on wet cloths soaked in wine and oil, and be wary of hot abscesses; once it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat with substances that excite growth.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In such a manner: take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make a poultice; and apply it to these wounds to promote flesh growth everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the congestion of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of the four things: grains, animals, stones from mines or similar things such as iron; seeds, such as peas, beans, and lentils; or flowing substances such as water and pus and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or any other substance that does not belong in the ear falls into it and does not grow inside the ear, place the ear towards the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a stone, then drop a little bit of violet oil or sesame oil to facilitate extraction; and make them sneeze with something that causes it, and plug their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and keep the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often the stone comes out through this treatment; and if it does not come out, treat it with fine forceps, which is described here:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the forceps, that is good; if not, use a fine needle to extract it; and if it does not come out even then, make a thread of silk and insert one end of the thread through the hole in the ear firmly, and plug what is around the thread with soft wax so that no air can enter with the thread; then pull it out completely, for often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take glue which birds use, and place some instrument suitable for it carefully, and put a little cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she cannot escape from all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear as for an abscess to come out easily and spasms; and the manner of cutting is that you first make the patient bleed from cephalic veins, and draw out the blood according to the measure of his strength, then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear in the fat where it hangs down; and let the cut be as a crescent moon until you reach the stone, then take it out according to your ability, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and treat him until he is well.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if this grain is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer the following subtle spatumile according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision of that tumor.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the tumor is moist due to moisture from the ear, until you have done many cases; then extract it with fine forceps and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In acute cases where it falls into the ear, the patient should use sneezing powders first, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie down on that same side where the pain is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it discharges because of that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not that way, take many stones according to the length of your thumb, and heat them slightly on the fire; then place one stone in the patient’s ear, and pour some water from another part with another stone over the stone which is in the ear; and do not stop putting stone upon stone until all the water comes out, and thus it will come out completely; and if you wish, take a reed, and put one end of it in the ear, and light the other end on fire until the softer part of the reed burns; then repeat with more reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said about the stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of the pest, if it is small like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, then use extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove that may be in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and if the cure is not effective, then it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sunlight: if any worms are apparent, take them out with fine forceps, and if none are seen, proceed according to this method:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And make it narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the finer end into the ear according to the severity of the patient's pain, then gradually form it all along the canal; do this frequently until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out willingly, plug around the canal with cotton as I have said for stones; and if they do not emerge as we have stated, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective against worms, which you will find in the treatment of distillations; and then distill your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument, whose form is as follows:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether of silver or brass, make a narrow sieve for the small holes, and above it place something to catch drops; and to press inside the distillation use an instrument of brass well made for this purpose, and if you want take a razor and wrap around the tip cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and what medicine you wish in the tube, and the tube should be in the ear; then put inside the razor all the cotton, and press with your hand gently until the oil is distilled to the bottom of the ear; and let the patient feel it within, and keep the distillation a little warm on the fire as when you distill into the ear; and beware that it is not too cold, for the medicine would be much worse.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the congestion of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	Some children are born without any hole in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to a blockage of an injury or flesh inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes come completely into the ear so that one cannot see it; and other times there is a small hole present which can be seen clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The one that comes completely inside and cannot be seen requires difficult treatment in many cases, and for the one you can see, you should put the patient's ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see hair visible, then perform this operation with spatula of which the form is as follows:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting in front and completely flat at the back so that it does not damage the ear; if the growth is flesh from inside the ear or from the ear's flesh, hold it with fine forceps and remove it gently until all the flesh is taken away.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the obstruction is in the ear, take a fine, light scraper and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it in the flesh of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the obstruction causing the patient pain in the ear, pierce it lightly, and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear; then place a tent in the ear according to the width of the opening, and apply Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for as many days as the wound takes to heal, and take a tent and moisten it with rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on top; and if you see the ear swollen, then you must remove the tent and replace it with another that is moistened in cerate made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling subsides; then continue to treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak a sponge and cloths in cold water, and place them on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This eyelid that comes in on the eyes when they are moist and dry, you must stretch it with forceps and tweezers, and cut off a piece from its root with a scalpel; then place crushed vitriol over the area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it does not peel off, then cauterize with a fine lentil-shaped cautery and the incision will heal with new growth; and often they need to be repaired because some part remains from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hailstones
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Often come onto the eyelids things that resemble hailstones in form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hail," and it is a gathering of thick moisture on the eyelid above and below; the treatment is as follows: observe if the hail moves from side to side, and it is easy to know; then cut widely, then gently peel each part, then grasp with tweezers, and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without piercing the skin slightly, do not cause any harm to the patient; and if the wound is large, sew it up with a stitch, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, make no effort, for the ointment will heal it soon and regenerate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the foreign body is inside the ear towards the upper part, turn the skin back, and extract the foreign body with forceps, and cut and squeeze from both sides; and if the skin is moved by the incision, it does no harm; and when the foreign body is removed, wash the eye with salt water, and treat the area that regenerates flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the grease of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is generated in the membranes of the eyes, and this happens more often with children than adults, and it greatly troubles their eyes, and they suffer from catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears hasten to their eyes; and for this reason they lie down on their faces immediately, and sleep like that, and their membranes below their eyebrows are moistened with a swelling and appearance covered by exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the area with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient places his head on your lap; then take a strip of linen and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount of exinach in each part, then place it over him; and press with your fingers from both sides so that the exinach gathers within the circle; then cut through the moisture with a sharp spatula making a slit no larger than the incision made for phlebotomy; and cut the membrane thoroughly until you reach the exinach; and in many cases, the exinach comes out of the slit, resembling a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull it out then in one piece of shredded cloth between your two hands when removing, and move your hand right and left until it is spread; and be careful not to add anything to the incision, so that you do not come all the way to the eyeball, so that you do not injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the excrement does not appear at the beginning of the incision, then enlarge the incision slightly until it appears; then pull it out as we have said, then moisten cloths in oil and water, and place them over the area, then bandage it.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are such people who grind salt and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat until he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he comes to the place of an abscess, treat with poultices soothingly until he is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the eyelids
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow in places other than where nature intended on the eyelids, and they become entangled, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases such as persistent tears and inflammation of the eyelids and conjunctiva, to the point that it can lead to the destruction of the eyes; and the treatment follows four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by medicine according to what is stated in the chapter on cautery, and also by incision and suturing or by cauterizing agents, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it turns properly, it is good; if not, put a needle along all the thread; and place this at the margin of the paper where the hair grows among these hairs, and draw the thread above all the paper, and turn it to the edge; then cut in the part below the paper, below the adjacent hairs, up to the entire spatumile from the large tear duct to the small; then extract the thread, and place below the paper a small tent of cotton and linen, then sew on the paper a figure of an egg, like the leaf of myrtle, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the size you wish to lift the paper which is prescribed for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is one who needs to cut a large quantity of the paper according to how the paper has been softened; then mark throughout the spatula on both lines that you have marked, and begin from the large tear down to small; and let one of the incisions be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the needle into one of the two corners of the wound, then skin it entirely; then sew together the two lips with a stitch of a fine thread, and wipe the blood, and bind the excess threads above both eyebrows to some sticky things if you wish to do so; and if not, then do not care about this, leave the stitches and the threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without stitching with drying and constricting substances, because the paper rises suddenly from the healing of the wound and its assembly, but the stitch is loose (as the ancients say), and these works are without fear; and there is another way: which is that you mark the paper in a shape as if it were the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, for three inches apart according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut those which rise above the small parts evenly according to the shape which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the parts are not even, then take a needle with its thread, and place it in the figure; and place one thread along the large wound margin, and the second thread along the small, and tie them together evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin on which you have sutured, as we have described, then close both edges of the wound with stitches, and heal it until it is healthy; and if an abscess comes from your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; but sometimes the hair on the paper turns: then you must use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one place and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of the canthus is as follows: convert the paper and cut into it according to what I have said, then make two canthi by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatumile are; sew at the two corners where you hold the threads; then carefully assemble one over the part that protrudes from the paper of the eye, and tighten the two canthi from both parts firmly; leave it thus for some days, and the skin which is stretched will die off, heal and regenerate, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, cut it with force, then treat until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, if the paper is raised, and the hairs will no longer grow there; and this is the form of the two canthi that you will make according to this figure, and according to this measure of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine needle and put a thin silk thread under it; then join the ends of the hair and tie them together finely, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then arrange another thin silk thread briefly in the socket, and tie the tips of the thread; then have the patient place his head on your hand; and do this near the sun so that the work is clearly visible, for it is a delicate and small operation; then insert the needle throughout the socket at the base of the hair next to it, and pierce through the skin quickly until you pull it over the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the socket, and place in the socket one or two or three or more hairs as there are; then remove your hand so that the hairs come out fully from the socket on the skin with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair is treated and the hair does not come out with it, pull the needle to the back along all the thread that you have inserted, until the needle comes out of the opening above and you can see it with your eye; then pull out the needle and the thread, close the eye and leave it closed for two days or three, until the hair hardens in its place and the flesh grows over; and if the hair is short, attach one long hair from natural hairs to it, and raise it along with the one you left behind, until it is raised up and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the pus of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or pus comes into the eye, there are two ways it can occur: one naturally, and the other unnaturally.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by sudden injury, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment is that you should split the wound open, separate its edges, and place linen tents inside, and keep it dressed until it heals; and you must not use in its care things that dry out and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness will return worse than before; but use softening things, such as fenugreek; and boil water with rue and flax seeds, and melt wax in some oil, and apply a poultice wrapped in a cloth, and treat it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you guard against it not healing according to its former form; and all the works we have mentioned are nothing but remedies for this illness, so that it does not return in its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is called "axacrati" in truth, and it has its nature and accidents.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidents come from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way of working is that you take a needle, which has double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and pierce from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread goes through two parts of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above all over the needle, and cover with one spatula breadth.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what is needed, it is good; if not, take the scraper and place it in the crevice, and turn the paper, and make II crevices on the inside of the paper; and let the ends of the II crevices be at the II angles of the incision that you have made, and make them into one angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is as the shape of a letter which has the name "I griesche"; then remove that flesh according to the quantity that its sides are acute underneath, from what is inside the paper, then join the II parts separated, and sew them together with linen thread; then treat it with what we have said about softening medicines, and bandages, until he is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a crevice or seam or cautery, it is necessary that you make a full incision underneath the hairs of the paper, as described above; then separate between the two sides of a bandage, as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters prepare with all their power how it may return the figure to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what requires work and instruments in many situations.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the sudden swelling of the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this swelling occurs in such a manner that the skin above is swollen with the white of the eye, and he cannot move or perform his natural works, then you must insert the tip of a razor under the skin, and lift it up; and stretch it with tweezers, until you cut off what is attached to the delicate spatumile, which should not be too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient cannot bear the delicate spatumile to scratch the eye; and make your incision, by which you peel off this assembly, lightly, so that the skin returns according to its natural form; and heal completely this assembly, and sometimes put salt water in the eye, and lift it with sweet water; then place between the skin and the eye a piece of linen, and put on the eye wool moistened abundantly with egg; and after the third day use salves and soothing things until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is according to two manners: it is nervous and similar to a hard surface, and another which is not nervous, but is like white congealed moisture, such that when one touches it with iron and thinks to pare it with pincers, it cannot be done; and both likenesses begin near the large tear duct, and grows little by little until it covers all of the sight and all of the light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient places their head in your lap, then works with their eyes; and lift the paper to your hand, then trim the nail with pincers of fine workmanship, and stretch it out; then take a needle, and put horsehair, or goat hair, or ox hair on it, and strong thread; and double the point of the needle slightly and insert it into the nail, and pierce all the way through the nail, and tie the nail with a thread and stretch it out, and shave off all the hair around the edge of the nail which encloses the rootlet and the silk to the tip, then cut the remaining part at the root of the tear duct with the fine spatula and small forceps, and leave the natural flesh of the tear duct, so that by the incision the body does not produce tears habitually; and sometimes they stretch out the nail only on the splinter, and with thread as we have said; then shave off all the fine layer beneath which is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And ensure that the spatula does not touch the thin membrane and break it, and that the probe is not punctured; after the incision, sprinkle a little ground sulfur into the eye, and apply a collyrium made of litargirius, and leave it until the next day; then treat it with whatever is necessary until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not attached to the nerve and you cannot insert the needle, and the hooks cannot enter, this condition of the nail is often treated with various medicines; and it grows as I have described in the division, and if you wish to cut it, then act cautiously regarding the patient's eye, and take a light, sharp spatula according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail gently from above, and if you see that it is becoming thinner and the tissue is pressing against it, then drip from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of litargirius and red collyrium mixed with ground sulfur, and plug the eye until the next day; then resume the work according to this same method until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If something is contrary in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then stop, and treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume work as before, until it is well.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the eyelid harms the eye greatly, then suspend it to the nail, and cut a part but not all, so that no tears come out; then drip into the eye red myrrh which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some people's eyes, red flesh sometimes grows and covers the pupil, restrains it under the eyelids and turns it outward, resembling a purple rose; and the treatment is that the patient places their head on your right side, then you work on the eyes, and carefully remove all that flesh with appropriate forceps, cutting until you reach the edge; then cut the first layer of flesh and continue cutting to the end with a razor, taking care not to injure the eye in the process; and make an incision as we described for nail cutting and small forces where the base is removed, as this chapter later demonstrates; when the incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, apply honey paste or drip red myrrh and similar caustic medicines into the eye; then place cotton soaked in egg white over the eye to prevent a hot abscess; if there remains any doubt of a hot abscess forming, treat it with things that soothe a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus handle flesh growing inside the eye by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you must still ease the treatment of each weak eye by the natural way; and by the accidental way, with iron work; and do not place your hand in any of these works until you see that this member can withstand that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Blood vessels are red and covered over the eye, and they impair vision in their work and weaken the eye all day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, first you must check if the eye, in which there is a blood vessel problem, is otherwise healthy except for this issue; then treat it as follows: instruct the patient to place their head on your hand, then suspend those vessels along the eyelid according to your knowledge, and let the eyelids be delicate double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two lancets be at different levels on the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then, when you approach these veins with force, gently wipe the blood hour by hour until you see the veins move away from the eye; and be careful not to scratch the eye with the tips of the spatulas, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not stop before these veins; and when you have done this, distill green and red collyrium into the eye to dissolve what remains of the ailment.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to collect all of this at that hour, apply a poultice to the eye with soothing ingredients to alleviate the pain of the eyes, and leave it for several days until the pain subsides and is sure of a warm abscess, then restart according to this manner as described before until it is healed; and this is the form of applying force:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The physician calls this type of fistula "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, there is a need to cut open the abscess where it should be opened, and drain all the moisture that is inside, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, remove it with all the instruments described here; it is called "aspre chief," and it should be made of iron tipped with points like a file as shown in this form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place over the site of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands and press gently until you know that the corruption has been removed; do this several times, then restore the area with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the area is sealed and flesh grows there, and the body of the bowel is sealed, and remains thus for forty days, and it does not renew itself and is not abscessed, and no bad accident occurs, know that he is healthy; if this is not so, then there is another intention to return the fistula to the anus according to this form: which is that you uncover the bone a second time with an instrument, and by using dry medicines, and when it becomes uncovered take one probe according to this form, and let the head of iron have three angles, and let the shaft be slender up to the top as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone near the temple, and keep your hand away from the eye one inch, then turn the probe completely until it penetrates the bone and the patient feels it because air enters if he holds his hand over his anus; and then restore the area with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when flesh grows and hardens the place, let the matter go to the anus; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the outlet of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is fully open and there is no disturbance or reduction in sight, you must bind the patient; then heal it, then apply cups to suck without striking, then place a poultice made of acacia, aloes, incense, and saffron on the eye, and then press the eye; and cover with bandages and cloths; the method for the cloths is that you take soft cloths and double each one four times, then place them one over another according to how much the eye needs; then press it from above with a hard bandage, and repeat the cups to suck without striking; then remove the cups and leave the eye pressed day and night, and if the poultice loosens, you must press it strongly again; then after a day and night, remove the poultice, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, repeat the poultices, cloths, bandages, and cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the tearing of a woven cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the woven cloth, it is opened up, and glue from papers is applied like resin grains, which is frightening to see; then if you wish to repair it, work as though you were inserting a needle at the base of the part below until reaching the upper part, then insert another needle where there is double thread from the lower edge; and make holes, leaving the first needle according to its position; then cut around the double thread area and tie one part of the woven cloth tightly, then remove the needle and apply wet wool over an abundance of egg white; leave it until the threads fall with the woven cloth, then care for the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; sometimes the wound is restrained by a circular piece of cloth on each side until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye shows great appearance [signs of distress], pierce it with a fine spatula that comes from the side of the eye, and let the watery humor flow out and lower the eye; then extract it until it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the socket of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but fluid gathered in the eye, resembling an inflow of water, but it is not actually water; and the manner of its appearance is that you seat the patient on a prepared and straight chair, then take his head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the fluid come up to your eyes; then if it remains there without descending and obscuring the light, know that it is an inflow, and if the descent of the fluid does not appear as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Situate the patient between your hands, then take the spatula and make an incision through the corneous skin along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneal tissue, until the pus comes out; and when it has come out, drop in hot honey mixed with water or water boiled with fenugreek and honey, then treat further as necessary until healed.
des aigues de l’oil	for eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have described the appearances of the eye conditions in the division, and what is necessary for piercing them; act according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should seat the patient between your crossed hands, away from light to avoid sunlight, and hold the healthy eye tightly with one hand; then place the paper of the affected eye in your left hand if it is the left eye, or in your right hand if it is the right eye; then take in your right hand, if the eye is the left, the instrument called "almagda," or in your left hand if the eye is the right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the cornea at a thickness of one thread from the white part of the eye near the tear duct, and gently insert the instrument called "almagda" vertically, turning your hand until it pierces the white part of the eye, and feel when the almagda reaches an empty space; and the length of the path of the almagda should be perfectly measured from the plumule to the end of the blackness; this is the cornea; you will see the bone on that paper through the clarity of the corneal tissue, then place the instrument where the fluid is, and press out along one pathway after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the fluid descends now, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, if the fluid rises again, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly inserted and does not rise further, gently twist it slightly; then add a small amount of powdered antimony to the fluid, and lift the eye from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place over the eye plugs made of wool soaked in rose oil and beaten egg whites, and secure them with a healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply it mixed with a lot of beaten egg whites.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if alum (a substance) cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, because there are people who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", which is of this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce only the conjunctiva, but do not go too deep, but do it delicately, and then put in the alum as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a dark room where they can sleep on their back in a dark place; and be careful of all movements, and give them light food, and do not move their head to the right or left, and bind them according to their condition until the third day; then unbind them in that same dark room, and test their vision, showing them some things, and then rebind them until the seventh day; and it should not be done during the time of treatment or immediately after incision, but you must wait because the fluid rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If abscesses come, that you loosen the eye before the seventh day, and direct it to him who lessens abscesses; and when it is appeased, then release the sight and place on it a bandage for some days, and let it be in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house little by little, and return to his usual habits; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in their country they make almond-shaped incisions, into which one suctions the fluid, but nevertheless I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor have I ever read about it in ancient books; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almonds, for those who do not recognize them; and they should be of proper brass:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the heads of these be of the same fineness, and the rear in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes flesh on the nose grows in various forms, some of which appear like many-footed scorpions; and there are such cases where it has flesh raised with reddish color, and there is smooth flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In the case of this smooth flesh that is not raised, you must have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and work his nostrils, and apply a needle to those parts, and draw them out straight; then proceed as much as you can sustain with the fine sharp spatula on one side, until you know that all of the flesh has been removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be cut, then operate with all the instruments finely and gently, so nothing remains; and if it overflows without your control, or if the abscess bursts, then treat it as is proper; and if these are malignant abscesses, then hurry and cauterize until the blood stops flowing and all the flesh is removed, then apply fresh and clear water or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose bleeds and moisture reaches up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if moisture does not come out as it should, know that there is flesh grown on the bone above, where the instrument cannot cut: then you must put a thick linen thread through it, tied with knots about an inch apart; and place the patient's finger in the nostril with some force, and pull out the odorant until it comes out of the nose into the mouth; and many times children at school do this, and it is an easy thing for one who wishes to do it; then hold one end that comes through the nostril with one hand, and the other end that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and pull them apart gently as they are in the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the new tissue has corrupted the old flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrupts all that remains of the flesh; and then place a plug of some sort in the nose for several days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, into which one distills oils and medicines through the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it may be made of silver or tin, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and the conduit should also be so; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full for purging the head; and have a handle at the top to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh over the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" is born on the head of the nose, and it grows until it becomes large enough to be visible; therefore, you must cut it at the beginning, remove all its roots, then apply the cautery or hot medicine over it. If you delay cutting it when it has grown too big, beware if it is hard, dark in color, or insensitive: do not touch it with iron because it is a chronic abscess, for when you cut it even once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess feels soft upon touching, not dark in color, and you see that all of it can be removed without fear, then empty the patient's body and remove it, treating the area with dry and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is broken and sewn up
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution for continuity comes to one of these cartilage works, it is little use, except in some men.
