Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, when this happens to anyone, examine if the wound is fresh with all its blood; then bring together the two edges into a seam, and treat it until it is healthy; and if the edges are separated from both sides, you must scrape all parts of their base until they heal, then join the two edges into a seam, and bind them, and apply powder made from dragon's blood and ground incense; and place the powders on a piece of strong adhesive plaster or another adhering plaster, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the stitching of the abdomen; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In some people, there is a hard abscess in the lips, resembling grains of wheat, smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, cut into each knot, take it with forceps, and cut it into each part; then fill the place after cutting vitriol that has been ground up, until the blood stops flowing; and then wash the area, and treat the wound with dry substances until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often on the gums grows attached flesh that the ancients call "albulus"; it is necessary to hold it with forceps, cut it at its root, and let the blood or pus run freely; then apply vitriol powder ground up, or other powders that constrict and dry; and if this flesh regrows after cutting, which often happens, cut it again, and cauterize: it will not regrow after cautery; these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of dirtiness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are gathered at the roots of the teeth in the mouth between the gums, crusts that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and rotten, until corruption reaches the gum, and they become foul-smelling; it is necessary for you to seat the patient between your hands, with their head in your lap, and extract the teeth or the crusts thoroughly, leaving nothing behind; and similarly deal with the blackness and greenish discoloration, and yellow and other stains until they are clean; if what needs to be removed is done at first attempt, it is good; if not, start again on the second day and the third, until you have completely extracted them; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments for extraction, according to what the work shows you, because the instruments used to remove teeth from between other teeth are different from those used when extracting a tooth entirely; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay pulling it as long as you can, for one must not do this; for it is a very high substance until there is no excuse for pulling.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is forced to pull the tooth, it is necessary that you be certain of the tooth causing pain.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the patient suffers from pain and believes it to be in the good tooth, and pulls out the healthy tooth; yet the pain does not depart by this means until the bad one is extracted, for we have already seen this happen with such patients; and when you are certain of the painful tooth, you should scrape around the tooth thoroughly with a spatula to protect the gum from all sides; then move it with your fingers or small forceps little by little until it is well loosened, then firmly secure the forceps; and hold the patient's head between your knees in sanctity, and keep it still so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and push into each side gently, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perforated and damaged, it is necessary to fill it with patches where the hole is; and you must extract it gently with pliers so that it does not break when extracting; and it is very important to work around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be very careful that you do not break it, and leave a part behind, and return to the patient because of the root's mischief greater pain than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful that you do not act as foolish practitioners do, who because of their haste and boldness sometimes break the tissue, and do not accomplish what we have mentioned; but instead they cause sometimes by this action serious illness from the roots that remain, or from the tissue they break, as often happens; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding continues, which often happens, fill the place with powdered vitriol; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments with which one moves the teeth first should have long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you extract the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick parts so that they do not bend when extracting, and they should be made of well-crafted iron, and should have teeth to hold the teeth.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in place after extraction, it is necessary to put cotton moistened with butter on the spot for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the wound is softened, then you can place the forceps called "algefri," which have tips that resemble a bird's beak; and they should be made inside like a file, and this is their form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to come out completely with these clamps, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root, and place the instrument which is called "althali," that is to say a scalpel, here is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps from there, that is good; if not, then aid with all the instruments, of which the forms come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one aids with this instrument that has two blades, of which here is its form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron tools which are mentioned earlier in the rationale of teeth, and of this instrument that resembles large clamps, here is its form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be such that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of bone are; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned; and the wise masters subtle find by themselves their instrument, according to what their work and the disease show them, for there are of such diseases where the ancients taught no instrument because of the diversity of cases; and if one breaks any of the cartilage or other bones, it will rot, so seek for instruments that should be used, which I have told you, and help with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-holding to hold the bone so it does not escape, but can be held and removed; then restore the place with medicines appropriate for this, and if there is putrefaction in the bone and it is small, remove it with all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth does not appear according to its natural position in the body, and the form is ugly, especially in virgin women, then you should know if the tooth has grown after another tooth, and it is not in its proper place, and cannot be smoothed or filed: then file it away; and if it is sideways with respect to the other teeth, take this instrument which here is described, and resembles a small beak, and let it be made of sharp iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut it bit by bit over several days due to the hardness of the tooth, and so as not to move the other teeth, and if it appears that you can file it, then file it with a tool like this one shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the file used to make needles; and file the tooth bit by bit over several days lightly, so that it does not move until it fits properly; then finish it at the end with any rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, then you must file down its roughness until it is even, so that it neither cuts the tongue nor impedes speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth grind together
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth grind together, either by percussion or falling, and the patient cannot bite down on what they are eating without having loose stools, and you have treated them with restrictive medicines but to no avail; then it is necessary to restrain them with a gold thread, for silver wire becomes green and rots, but gold never moves. And let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; if you wish to set the teeth straight, take the thread and wind it doubly between two healthy teeth, then place the end between the misaligned teeth, whether there is one or several, carefully until you reach a healthy tooth on the other side. Then continue covering with the thread back to where you started, and pull your hand carefully and skillfully so that nothing moves; and let the ligature be at the root of the tooth so it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the tooth with pliers and assemble it, and place it between healthy teeth so that it does not bite the tongue; then leave it as tight as possible until it can stay, and if it loosens or the wire comes off, tighten it with another wire; it will remain and serve in this way for its entire time, and this is the form of the tooth and the shape of the arrangement of two healthy teeth and two bad ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, put another in its place, fresh for fresh, as we have said; and do not intervene with anyone who is not wise and skilled, and sometimes one makes the form of a tooth from a piece of whalebone, and places it where the deficiency is, and tightens it as we have said, and it remains and serves for such a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	There is sometimes this ligament that comes from under the tongue either by nature at birth; or by accident of a wound that has healed; and the procedure is such that you work on the mouth of the patient, and hold his head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament widely, until the tongue is detached from its base, and if there is hardness or knot, which is due to sudden healing of a wound, use an instrument like a hook and cut it broadly as well; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, near the artery below; and when you have finished, lift the area with rose water and aloe, or cold water, then place under the tongue a dressing of linen; and change the bandage each night so that the wound does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, place over the area ground vitriol; and if it affects the blood, then cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other treatments until he is well.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it as a dusky or black or hard color and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is an ulcer; and if it inclines towards phlegm and there is moisture, then apply lancing, and cut it with a fine scalpel, and release it from both sides; and if the blood affects your work, place over it ground vitriol until it is constricted, then return to your work as long as you keep all strength; then lift the area gently and carefully, and treat it with other treatments until he is well.
des apostemes de la gorge	abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes in the throat there come lumps which are called "godath," and they are properly referred to as the two tonsils, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and if they are not healed, take care: if these abscesses are hard with little sensation and a dark color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is swollen, do not touch them with iron, nor let blood; but leave them until they turn black, and then you will remove them, as they will naturally fall off; and if they have a white color and the root is delicate, prepare the instrument to cut, but first observe whether the abscess lies at rest and has subsided.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit before the sun, and his shoulders in your sight, and work on his mouth and press the tongue down with all the instrument, which is of this form; and it should be made of silver or fine brass like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	As you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see an abscess, take a lancet and insert it into the almond-shaped area, and pull out more than you can; then draw some substance from the wound with it, then close it with the instrument, which is of this form, resembling a forceps; and yet the head is curved, one part to another, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, cut it with pliers, of which here is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side and named on the other; and when you have cut one of the glands, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot, soothing water, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with warm water containing pomegranate peels or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped; then heal it until he is well; and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two glands, so cut them as you would the two glands equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman who had an abscess that was born inside her throat, which is to say the tonsil abscess; and it had almost completely closed off her entire throat, so the woman could not breathe due to the blocked passage, nor eat or drink, and she would have died if she remained in this state for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had risen so high that it had forced two inches through each of the two openings of the anus.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then and inserted a lancet into one of them, pushing it out forcefully, and extracted a large portion of pus; then I repeated the procedure on the other opening of the anus, opened her mouth, and pressed her tongue; after that, I inserted the lancet into the abscesses again, removed part of it, but only a little blood came out; thus, the throat conduit of the woman was cleared, and she now began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to incise this abscess for a long time; the abscess kept growing back quickly, filling up the space that I had emptied until it became large again; then I treated it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it remained without growing further; and I left these parts, and do not know what God did for her after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When rheum descends into the eye and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is detached and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have described in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the large abscesses are alleviated, but they are subtle, then you must cut them; and those that are round and assembled and are not elongated; and if they are bloody or of a dusky color or black, then you must avoid cutting them.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its blueness and length, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument of which we made mention above; then place the lancet in the uvula, and draw it down, and cut at the point where the two instruments that I mentioned for cutting the two tonsils are used.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut beyond the excess that is outside the natural boundary; for if you cut more, it will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said about cutting the two tonsils, and treat it until it heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears the cutting, it is necessary that you use cunning in the cautery to calm his fearful senses.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of the cautery is sharp heat.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient place their head on your lap, and then press the tongue with the instrument we mentioned in the chapter of cautery, and cover it with sharp vinegar, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and apply this method to the use of this instrument, as follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place on the head a container where the medicine is placed, as much as fits in a spoon, and put the instrument over all the medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on their side so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine without it reaching the throat or dripping; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour until you see it has taken effect and the movements of the medicine have ceased; if you wish, take cotton and wrap some around an instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument with the cotton on top of the eyelid so that the cotton adheres to the eye; do this often until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and after four or five days remove it. If you need to restart the cautery with the medicine, do so; after the cautery, wipe around the eye with cotton wrapped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine area; have them rinse with cold water and gargle until they are well.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective than incision or cautery; if it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take camphor and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and lavender and similar herbs, and combine them all or some of them in one pot, and add salt, and bring to a boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot have an instrument pointed according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or bronze, and one end of the instrument should be placed in the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the affected area through the vein, until the ulcer is necrotized; then repeat this often, until the ulcer dries up, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, as many things can happen; and do not perform it unless there is a decline in a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a chain and place inside the head an egg yolk so that the patient’s mouth does not get too hot; for the egg yolk does not let the vapor weigh down the mouth, and this is both a good remedy and safe.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or spine of fish, or something else, gets stuck in the throat. Therefore, you should extract what you can see and press the tongue with sunlight on all sides so that the object moves; and for what is hidden deep inside the throat, you must induce vomiting as if the food were cooked in the stomach; perhaps this will cause the foreign object to come out by vomiting; or have the patient swallow a piece of sponge, or some seaweed, or lettuce root, or dry bread; tie a thread to the sponge and then make them swallow it; when it reaches its place, it will stick, and then pull it out. And if none of these methods work, take this instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and hold the head up high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, or choking may occur, nor force the bone inside; move the patient to where they will insert the instrument, because it should be moved where the thing is hard; if inserted down, pull it out evenly, until it is entirely out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the blood is treated, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look into the patient's throat in the sunlight, pressing their tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, draw it out with a small hook, or with fine forceps that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that is not effective, take a hooked cane and insert it into the patient's throat, then place a hot iron on the hook of the cane, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is stained with water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, work it in the mouth, and pour it down to be swallowed, and move it with your hand frequently; and as soon as the blood feels the water, it falls.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then suffume the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument I mentioned for the fumigation of grapes; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of fumigation is that you take one pot with live coals, and cover it with a perforated lid, and through that hole place the head of the instrument; then pour in your fumigation, and have the patient put the end into their mouth, and close the mouth so that no smoke escapes but goes up to the blood; and now the blood will fall out, and if it does not fall, restart the fumigation several times; and allow the patient thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, and do not drink water; and then by this governance it is necessary for it to come forth forcefully.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the blood, when it can be seen, resembles curved tongs for entering into the throat; and it has the appearance of a bird's beak, and there are rough edges like a file, so that what it grasps, it cannot let go; and here is its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscesses, according to what the memory brings forth later from one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and this is in two ways, one of which is in its likeness itself, and from what it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for abscesses of the head are different from those of the buttocks, and abscesses of the flesh area are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses that one must not pierce until the swelling is complete according to its fulfillment; and there are also such as should be pierced when they are hardened, and do not die off according to their completion, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and one lets it remain until it is rotten around, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, thus causing contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay puncturing it until it is deadened, it will harm the principal limb; when it is near the fundament, pierce it before it becomes necrotic; and it is not right to puncture an abscess that has not fully digested, except for one near the fundament, so that it does not become rotten, and extends inside, and a fistula comes about; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of puncturing an abscess that has become necrotic according to its completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the subsidence of fever, and the diminishment of pain and redness, and the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you perform the puncturing where the abscess depends most, and where it appears soft; and let the puncture be along the body, and if the abscesses are on the hands or feet, at joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equally where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In cases of bleeding, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the flesh, it is better to wait until it is confirmed to be in complete resolution before proceeding with puncture, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you puncture it before then, the body of its venom will be prolonged, and it will be full of much filth; and by chance the lips and depths of it may harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that needs to be punctured according to the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should treat small abscesses with small punctures; and large abscesses with large punctures, and many incisions according to the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses that require cutting deeply, and excising; when they have become as hard as leather, and softened, then you should treat them as you would boils: and if there are those that are cut into three angles, and some that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, as in abscesses on the gums; and if there are those where a round incision is made, and other cuts and similar excisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have a superficial subcutaneous abscess should be fully punctured by you; and when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at that moment, but draw out some of it; then stopper the abscess until the next day, then extract something again; do this gradually over many times, until all the pus comes out; similarly if the patient is weak, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old men who are feeble.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the pus sometimes suddenly stops coming out with the pus, which by chance can kill the patient, and you would not be blamed for it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have punctured your abscess, wash the wound, and check if the abscess wound is small; if it is a full incision, then apply lint or old cotton to it; and if it is large abscesses, and there are many openings, then place a tent in each so that they come together; and if you have cut into the skin of the abscess and sewn around it, then fill it with old linen fluff or dry lint without moisture, and tie it up for three days; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, administer cold and soothing remedies, and wet a cloth, placing it on the bleeding area multiple times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, apply proper treatment and care, and use the powders I have mentioned earlier in this book. If it is winter and the area where the abscess is located is very tense, you should place tents and cloths soaked in wine and warm oil; and if it is summer and the area is fleshy, you should put on cloths soaked in water and oil, or cold wine and oil, for three days as we have said. Then loosen the abscess, dry it, and treat it properly until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this one must know universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	Of sweats
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	For small abscesses in the head come in various forms, like the feathers of a goose, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and have moisture like pus; and there are others that are hard and stony to the touch, and there is no doubt unless the artery opposes it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work on the waist is such that you should try all the instruments called "entromissoire," of which the forms are shown hereafter, what they contain.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if there is moisture, then he splits it from above along the length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied out, then scrape away without leaving any part of the skin that contained the moisture, for it returns quickly if anything is left; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is available; if not, in water and vinegar, and apply to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who are delayed at night should do this.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then reuse the cotton as before on the second day, and on the third, until you know for certain that it does not remain overnight; then treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds in fat, cut it according to this form, along its length; and pour on your onions, and strip off all around the skin, and put all your effort into draining through the coat where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, do as I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same for an abscess if it is stony, and in cutting and curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when you cut into a stony abscess and moisten it, it becomes easier, for they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses occur on the head where there is no moisture, and I encountered such an abscess in the head of an old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if one had struck it with force, it would have caused injury like striking a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming to the head, whether those that come at the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the incision should always be made in the lowest place, so that the pus may exit; and treat them as is appropriate.
des scrophules	scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	This type of abscess often occurs in the neck, and sometimes below the armpits, and also in angles, and at times they appear elsewhere on the body, and are very numerous, growing one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own area, as the knot and the head abscess are, as we have said; and there are many similarities to these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that are malignant and do not wish to obey [the treatment].
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those that you see are well disposed for touching, and resemble the color of the skin, and are not hard against any part nor deep in the neck veins or arteries or conduit; then it is necessary to cut above it, and peel off from each side, and stretch the two lips of the wound with needles if needed, as we have said about abscesses on the head; and make small incisions, and be sure not to cut a nerve or vein, and do not let the spatula become sharp or cutting, so that your hand does not slip, and do not go too far in, lest you cut what should not be cut.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work on it, place in the wound vitriol ground up, or some powders that constrict blood, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and then begin to treat it.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is constricted, return to your work until you complete it; then seek with your proper index if there remain any small swellings, and cut them and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the swelling, you must not cut that swelling at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire boil, then you must bring together the two edges of the wound and sew them now, since there is no excess tissue due to the size of the boil.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	Then you must focus on cutting the root of it, extracting the pus, and sewing as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For those boils that contain excess tissue, pierce where it appears to be most mature; and puncture them as we described earlier, depending on the situation, then administer dressings with ointments and similar treatments so that they do not corrupt what remains from the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, treat with healing ointment until it is healed.
de squinance	of contusion
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote about the incision of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have contusions, it is necessary to avoid the incision of the throat fold known as "epiglottis"; and one should not give aid through this method, because all the veins and phlegm of the patient are at risk for those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the phlegm channel, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the danger of choking.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we make a small incision across it between three or four circles, between two of them or according to the size of the incision on the surface, not in the cartilage; and these areas are suitable for cutting the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from end to end.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, he should stretch the skin of the neck to its full thickness, then cut through until he reaches the windpipe; and avoid the vessels filled with blood, if you see anything unusual, and then cut the surface as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the sectioning of the fluid in the windpipe which will shoot forth from the place that is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for which strangulation is feared, bring together the two lips of the wound of the heart, and sew it all up without the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote tissue growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dying, and death approaches.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he will breathe through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and for this reason, the elders commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness passes, which takes three or four days, and then they command it to be sewn up and cleaned until it is clean; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a knife and stuck it in her throat, cutting part of the windpipe; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I examined the wound and found the blood that had come out, and realized that she had not cut any vein or vital artery but rather the wind was escaping through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened and sewed up the wound, and treated it until she was healed; and nothing worse happened to the lady than that her voice became hoarse, and she returned later to her usual state; therefore I say that there is no need to fear in cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called a "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in the color of a blackbird; and it often occurs in women; and it comes in two ways: natural, and accidental; the natural one does not have a swelling.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one comes in two ways, of which one is similar to our fat, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from us due to an artery; and there is fear, and it does not befit to operate except on those that are small, and prove and search throughout the interior: if you find it as our fat, and cannot reach any vein, then cut it like one cuts fat, and remove its entire covering, if there is any; and seek quickly, and cure it properly as needed until it is completely healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways from us, of which I will tell all the similarities; and now it is necessary that I speak about all the differences that exist between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the fever and heat persist until the boiling is past, and the putrefaction is completed; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With us there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a swelling, which is its own sac and matches the color of the skin, and begins like a pimple and grows large; and they are similar in appearance, either hard or soft, and many colors as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the knot, that you test and inquire first about all the instruments which are called "entromissoire", according to what their form will come in the chapter which is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses is that you take the place where it is most moist in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, as befitting the size of the abscess; then withdraw the entromissoire, and beware when it comes to force.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture comes running out cut, whatever color it has, proceed as I said for the other abscesses; and if after the entromissoire no moisture comes out, know that it is greasy, then make an incision in a cross shape, take it with pincers, and lightly scrape from each side and be careful of the skin where it lies so you draw it whole with the knot; and if you cannot draw it whole, then draw it piece by piece so nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains there, the pus will return many times; and if a little remains and the blood pains it, apply the wound with some corrosive powder substances, and stretch the wound, and place hot poultices to ease the abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the pus is great, sew together both edges of the wound, and treat it as one who generates flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the wound resists or is contrary to other treatments, hurry and apply a place of broiled vitriol, and leave it for two days or three, until the wound becomes rotten, and let the blood boil; then return to scraping what remains of the pus.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of instruments used for probing, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three square ones called "albaret," and one called "breb," which come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses of fistulas; and they are like the needles used to sew sorcerers, made of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and those with a yellow hue are more valuable, and for probing the curves of fistulas, those coated in black pitch are preferred; and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of hooks are very diverse, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are hooks that have two curves in three different ways; and there are hooks that have three curves, and they are also in three different ways; and there are hooks with two curves, and some with only one curve, and these too are in three different ways; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The tip of these tools that one uses to cut are sharp, and some do not cut from both sides, for which one peels the skin, so as not to cut into the vein or nerve; and among these there are lancets with handles, such that the patient does not feel them when opening abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them only in soft flesh areas like legs, arms, breasts, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another tool smaller, resembling a splinter remover, according to this form, for stopping blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed sometimes at the place where the veins are cut, and at the arteries, and sometimes follow this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so much that they seem like women's breasts; and remain ugly and swollen, and if one wishes to treat them, it must be done according to this form from this line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat and fill the wound with flesh-generating medicine, then join the two edges of the wound by suturing, and treat it until it is healed; and if the breast sags down and becomes soft due to its size as happens in women, cut it into two parts from above through two similar incisions, so that one end connects to the other at both ends, such that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form from this line b to the line g; then scrape off the skin between the two edges and remove the fat, and apply the treatment we have mentioned regarding suturing and powders, as well as what is necessary for healing, until it is healed; and if it does not heal or the incision is not fully made because the patient does not want to rest or due to excessive bleeding, you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in a corrosive ointment; let it remain there until it consumes the remaining tissue and fat, then treat it until it heals.
des apostemes des asselles	abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the buttocks are like hard scrofulous lumps containing sides, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is emptied out, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat it with ointment as needed until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles a scrofula, then cut it as we have said for incisions of scrofulas, and if the wound discharges pus, then treat it with cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above it is sealed, abscesses often occur; similarly, this happens when a vein is swollen and an abscess forms. And if you know it to be from the artery, the abscess will be long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, you sense tightness; and when it comes from the vein, it appears softer and closer to the surface; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits, around the angles of the body, on the neck, and in many other places, and it is very large.
