Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, it is necessary to avoid treatment with iron, and those who are at risk should also avoid it. In cases of arterial swelling, make an incision above the skin along its length; then work carefully around the arteries, separating them from the tissues until they are exposed; then insert a needle underneath the area, piercing through to the other side, and tie off the artery with double thread as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries located in the temples. Then prick between the two threads with an intercalary needle so that blood flows out from there; loosen the abscess accordingly; then apply a poultice made from herbs until the ligature falls off; and if the swelling is due to the vein, you should mark the area of the abscess on the skin with your hand, then insert the needle underneath where your hand marks it, piercing through, using double thread; tie off the abscess as I have instructed, securing one end of each of the two threads at the two ends of the stitch; if you doubt that the thread might come out, insert another needle along the entire length of the abscess below the first incision, and secure all the threads in four places. Then cut open the abscess until the excess matter flows out; then remove any excess heart tissue while leaving what is bound behind. Finally, apply a moist bandage soaked in wine and oil, followed by dressings and ointments as needed until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses can occur in the artery and vein, abscesses also affect the nerves when they are injured, or from excessive labor, and similar circumstances.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and elbows and in all places where there are joints, and these are severe abscesses, and their color resembles the color of the skin, and they cause intense pain; and when they are pressed firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not throughout the body but near the heart; and it does not move forward or backward, nor side to side, and those that are in joints must not be cut with an instrument: for fear of causing contraction; and those on the head or forehead, incise the skin at the suture.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with pincers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it on a hook, scrape it out, then remove it and close the wound by stitching, and treat it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	large hanging mouths
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes this condition occurs in the abdomen and not elsewhere, and it is called a "fungus" due to its resemblance, with subtle roots and large bases; there are small ones and very large ones. I saw a person who had two of these in their abdomen that looked more like fungi than anything else, with no difference, they were white, had fine roots, were rather split, and moisture corroded them quickly.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I weighed them and found the first one to be eighteen ounces in weight, and the second six [ounces], and the work in cutting is such that you should observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist with a fine texture; then cut it wide with the scalpel, and have the cautery by fire ready at hand.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For when cutting there are often excessive flows of blood, and if the blood overpowers you, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient terrified and afraid of the iron incision, take a well-made linen thread, tie it around the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; then remove it, but do not stop tying the linen thread until you cut the artery, and proceed carefully with the work; and if the roots are thick, be wary when cutting, especially regarding the abdomen, but you may well cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not regrow; then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the tendon which is of red color and poor texture and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an embedded abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers shortly thereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the swelling subsides
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the swelling comes from a cautery on a wound or fissure on the surface, and it is on the abdomen and some boils appear, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries as mentioned before, or from gas; and if this is due to a rupture of the skin and an opening in the belly, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the skin, it is a light matter without pain, and clearly has multiple outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if this is due to the opening of the intestine, then it is more varied, and when it is pressed at its sides it swells up, and then subsides, and perhaps it is hard, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and for heavy work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and you can easily tell when you press it in your hand, as it does not resist; and if it is due to blood, it becomes apparent through these signs of large and hard abscesses, which are fixed according to a certain amount; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft upon touching, and the work involves observing whether the appearance is that of arterial or venous blood, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear about it, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bladder, you must instruct the patient to hold his breath, lie flat, and then tie a bandage all around the abdomen; then have him lie quietly between your hands, then work around the area where you marked with the entire spatula; then extend half of the abscess above the large uncinate ligament; then bind it tightly with strong thread or a firm silk cord, making sure that the knots are secure; then work on the extended half of the abscess over the bandage, place your index finger inside, and seek the intestine; if you find it caught in the binding, loosen it, and pull the intestine out of the belly; if you find the bladder, grasp it with a clamp, and cut off any excess tissue; if an artery or vein obstructs your work, proceed gently, then return to your task and take two needles, placing two threads through them, and place the needles in a cross shape where you intend to pierce; then stretch the abscess into four parts over the needles, and if needed, remove the needles once the area has softened and become necrotic, then cut away the dead tissue, cure it as we have said, extract any blood or moisture you find, and treat the wound as necessary, and suture it.
dou chancre	of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division about the similarities of ulcers, and how one should treat them with medicines, and how one should avoid treatment with iron; and we say that an ulcer originates in a wet area, and there is great caution in its treatment. The ancients said that when ulcers are in places where they can be scraped out like those found in the breasts, on the thigh, and in similar areas, you should remove them entirely when they are in their beginning stage; but when they are large and old, one must not approach them, for I have never seen any heal from such treatment; nor has anyone ever healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment, when it is in a place where it can be removed as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile if necessary; then make the patient fast if there is obvious repletion; then position the patient properly for the procedure; then apply your forceps to the ulcer and remove all hair around it, removing everything without leaving anything behind; let the blood flow freely and press firmly on the area with your hand or something else; if the bleeding from the wound disagrees with cutting an artery or vein, cauterize until the bleeding stops; then treat further as needed until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of hydropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already described in the division the appearances of hydropsy, and how the accumulation of water is formed, and the signs of each appearance, and the cure that is performed with medicines, and that which is cured by iron: it is called 'eclites' solely; and one should not touch with iron in these two appearances: that is to say, tympanites and yposarche, because it is a lethal thing; therefore when you treat this appearance of hydropsy which is called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not succeed, then look if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides hydropsy, such as coughing and diarrhea and similar things; do not touch with iron in these cases, because there is uncertainty; and if you see that the patient is of strong constitution, and he has no other illness than hydropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then proceed thus: lift the patient straight up in your hands, and the assistants press the belly by pushing out the water to the lowest part of the abdomen, then take the spatumile according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be cuts from two sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	With a point, and ensure that it does not go so deep as to reach the intestines when inserted, nor should it bleed; then observe if the dropsy is towards the intestines: you must cut above the navel three fingers wide from beneath the rib; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, make your incision on the left side of the navel three fingers; and if it is due to mucus, make it on the right side, and the patient should not lie on the incision so that the excesses do not flow to a weak spot; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and pull out your hand throughout the spatumile between the skin and the subcutaneous layer as much as when stripping off like a quarter of an inch around; then puncture the subcutaneous tissue until the spatumile comes to the place where water is, which is the location of the fluid, then draw it forth, and insert this instrument whose form follows:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a fine silver chain, and is made of iron or brass light, and has in the middle part one small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two on another side, and one on another; and the head is shaped like a feather quill, and this is the form of the incision which the scribe makes when cutting the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the alembic, such that when the instrument comes to the liquid, it now descends upon the instrument; empty then half or a third of it, for if you empty more than necessary at this hour, perhaps the patient may die from the resolution of their spirit by the weapon, or they faint, or approach death; but empty according to the quantity of its strength, and according to what the disposition of the patient's strength signifies, and his pulses; then draw out the instrument and retain the liquid, and it is now retained for the heart which stops up the hole that is above the surface, of which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then reinsert the instrument another day if you see the patient suffering from this, and draw out a small quantity of liquid; do this some days, and guard against fooling around too much as it may remain but a little bit of liquid.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and leave him much moisture, then cure with burial soil or hot sand, and by much sweating or bath and in the sun, and have him refrain from drinking; and treat with drying medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the moisture, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	about the numbness of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born without an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary to pierce it immediately throughout the spatumile very finely according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place in the orifice a fine cloth plug, and tie it securely for three days or four, and when he wishes to urinate, remove the plug so that he may urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps no such plug is necessary, for the urine which comes forth does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose orifice is small should be treated with a cloth plug of flax, as we have said, and it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the orifice in its place are afflicted, for some are born with the orifice at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis upward; and they cannot copulate because the matter cannot reach the testicles, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies supine on their back, then place the tip of the rod against it and position it as with the thickness of a pen feather, so that the hole fits exactly in the middle, as is appropriate; and be wary of blood loss which often occurs, and if it happens, stop the bleeding with what stops blood, and treat the wound until he is healed.
des pustules de la verge	pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these blisters appear on the penis, and they have an ugly appearance; there are both malignant and non-malignant ones among them; you must pierce them with a fine lancet, clean and clear them all, then apply cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; afterwards cure it with diafinicon ointment until he is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of foul color and spreading, then you must apply a cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the ulcer is deep in the flesh, with part inside the skin and part outside, then you must remove the part of the ulcer that is inside first; and when it is adhered, treat it as being outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, the flesh of the ulcer is not certain to heal without being pierced, and blackness and corruption come into the flesh and in the genitals; thus you must remove all that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster made from pomegranate bark and wine, and continue treating it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, then treat with the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps in two conditions simultaneously: namely, bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary to insert a lead tube into the urethra through which the patient can urinate; and when hair forms on the head of the uncircumcised penis due to injury or abscess, then you must cauterize with a sharp instrument until the ligament is loosened, and free the head of the penis from all sides; if it is difficult to describe this precisely, then cauterize slightly at the top of the penis and skin with a spatumile, then carefully separate them and place a fine linen cloth moistened in cold water between them so that hair does not form again.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like the separation of continuity as other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work by our will, and especially on children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the least harmful to their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they did not practice it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the majority of masters and surgeons who performed circumcision around the time of puberty, and with great force, and all in one attempt; it was painful because there were two layers, and by chance they might cut the upper layer while leaving the lower.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now it must be cut back, and the pain is doubled, and in the cleaning of the nail there is no certainty about the tip of the member; and when filing the nail by chance the tool slips, and the work runs rough, and many times they are born such that they do not need cleaning and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleaning that is done with force to the entire length of the filament, I have found the goodness through experiment, for the force cuts precisely both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, cut evenly in one smooth motion; but the filament should be tight around the skin; and the manner of the first work is that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only tying the filament around the shaft simply, then let him enjoy it in any way possible; then place it straight between your hands, and move the filaments between your hands or feet so the child does not see them nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the shaft and blow at its head, lifting it up until the tip of the shaft is raised; then clean thoroughly from the accumulated dirt, then tie a double thread over the spot, then tie below the pocket to another filament; hold it by two fingers through the second binding in the pouch and at the index finger, cut between the two filaments, then lift the head quickly and pull it up; let the blood drip drop by drop because this is slow; place powder upon it and over the powder a piece of cloth glued with an egg white mixed with rose water, seasoned well with fresh rose oil, leave it on until the next day, and care for it in another manner as long as it needs healing.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the force for cleansing is as follows: the two edges should be blunt and should be equally thick as the blade.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in cleansing is when the pus inside goes to the incision; then it is necessary that you extend it to your nail, just as one would an abscessed boil; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it to your nail, hold it with forceps, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass three days, and the area below the shaft is swollen, let it be until the abscesses are sufficiently reduced, and lightly scrape it; then cut as you can move, and avoid the part of the shaft, so that it does no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat then the wound with powder, which we have mentioned in the chapter on powders, and if it cuts into the heart too much, and goes beyond measure, it will not harm; treat it then as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	from the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the accumulation of stones, or congealed blood, or boils, or dead flesh, or similar things, as we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine does not flow freely, and you see that the retention is caused by a stone which is lodged at the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to be seated on his knees; and place his feet on his back, and stretch out his belly from above the back, and have the patient strain his alaina (a term possibly referring to abdominal muscles) as much as he can; and thus the neck of the bladder is constrained to express the stone upwards, causing the urine to flow freely; and if it does not come forth, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instruments that are called "syringe", here is its form: it should be made of fine light silver threads, like a feather of an eagle; and its tube should be one palm in length and half, and should be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method of releasing urine is that you take a double thread and tie at the top a piece of wool or cotton, and put the end of the thread into the syringe; then trim the excess wool and push it all the way to the top of the syringe, then grease the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk albumin, and have the patient sit on a stool, and anoint the bladder and penis with moist olive oil and cold water; then gently place the syringe into the penis until it reaches the base, then fold the penis over towards the body; then push the syringe forward to the bladder, and when the patient feels it reach the empty space, and this is not done according to this order unless for the reason that where you guide it is crooked; then pull out the thread piece by piece, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out and let the urine flow; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and relieve the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When blood or pus comes to the bladder and putrefaction gathers there, and you wish to introduce liquids and medicines, use all the instruments that are called "clepsydre," and this is their form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed and has III openings: II on one side, and I on the other, as you see; and the place where the medicine goes should be such that it stops up the tube well so that no moisture can be drawn out or pushed in; and when you wish to introduce your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the catheter into the moisture, and draw with the syringe which is inside; thus you will draw the moisture into the catheter, and then push it back forcefully; thus the moisture will enter again, reaching the bladder so that the patient can feel it; this is the form of a subtle enema used to administer an enema to the bladder: here it is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or brass, and the head is higher; and below near the breast where the ligament falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture with which you wish to enema the bladder, then tie between the two breasts tightly with a good double thread, and heat the pot of that moisture over the fire; then insert the head of the enema into the penis, then press your hand on the bladder gradually until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and perforate it neatly around; then tie a strong thread through these holes, then join the circle as one joins a tile, and put inside what you wish of oil and moisture and water, and tie to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand gradually until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed in the division the methods of stones and their extraction along with medicines; and I have explained the difference between a stone generated in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in which types of stones one should operate for cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is generated in the bladder happens more often to children, and this is a sign that the urine jumps from the bladder similar to acute urine in its subtlety; and one can clearly see sand, and the patient's penis becomes inflamed, and it hurts him many times, and then subsides; and there are many such attacks at the foundation; and the healing of children until they are four years old is much easier, and it is very difficult for the elderly, and it is moderate for young adults, those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is less severe for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, to draw out all the feces that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes hinders in finding the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and lift him up and move toward his back so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes it comes from a high place; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands should be behind his thighs, so that the bladder is completely tilted downward; then search for and touch inside; if you feel the stone in its place, now hurry to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall with the touch of everything, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand if the patient is a woman, or your middle finger if the patient is an adult male; and insert it into his rectum, and search for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, guide it to the neck of the bladder; then press on your finger, and push it out where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to stretch out his right hand towards the groin area, and with his left hand remove the skin that is underneath the groin at the part where one makes a cut; then place the spatula cutting edge first, which is its shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make an incision between the groin and the buttocks, not in the middle but on the side of the left thigh; and let it be straight across the stone, and both ends should be close to the buttocks, and let the cut be wide at the top, narrow within, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure will cause the buttock muscles to jump out without effort; and know that there are some stones with angles and edges: these are difficult to remove; and there are others that lie flat, like a clover leaf, round, from which removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For those who have angles and margins, make the circumference larger; and if it does not jump, then you must squeeze with pincers that are like a file at the top to move the stone so that it does not escape; or insert an instrument curved at the tip underneath; and if you cannot manage it thus, enlarge the bladder's neck, and if blood flows, stop it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, push out the largest first into the bladder’s neck, then proceed upwards, then draw out forcefully, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then you must observe it carefully and make a larger incision.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes out too quickly so that the wound cannot heal properly; but nonetheless, you must strive to draw it out, using pincers as needed, until you remove it piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloes and dragon's blood, then press it firmly, and place a moist cloth over it in oil and wine, or in rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then lift the patient onto his shoulder, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, wash the area very well with oil and water, then treat it with diafinicon ointment and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses and ulcers come in the wound, and clots of blood in the bladder, which cause retention of urine, which is known to happen in this manner that without straining it does not pass: apply your hand to the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains there, it will corrode the bladder and rot; then wash the wound with water and moss and silk, and aid him in all ways you know until he is healed; and it is necessary that every time you treat him, you tie his two thighs together, and apply medicines to the area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small and it is in the channel of the penis, stuck inside so that urine cannot escape; then treat this as I say, cut it many times, and by this treatment it is excused from the cutting.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tested this in this way.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron fork according to this form and let it have three prongs fixed in one handle:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take some thread and tie it around the penis below the stone so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then gently insert the fork into the penis until it reaches the stone; and rotate the fork with your hand on the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; urine will soon come out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is immediately broken, and the urine comes out with it, and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie a thread under the stone and another above, then cut the penis along the stone between the two threads, then extract the urine, and loosen the knot, and clean the clotted blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of women's stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone appears in women, and if it does occur, the treatment is difficult, and it is prohibited for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a knowledgeable woman who will expose herself to doctors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more hard than the stone of the man, so it requires deeper cutting, and great fear there is. And if necessity comes to these, then it must be that you take a midwife well knowing, and at pains find one, and if you do not find her, do not seek a wise cast; and present to her a bailiff well wise in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command that she make what you command concerning the inquiry of the stone; and carefully look if the woman is virgin: then it must push her thumb to the fundament and seek the stone; and if she finds it, constrain it under her thumb, and recommend that she pushes her thumb into where the patient has pain, and seeks and presses her left hand firmly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder down to underneath, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut above the stone at the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the rectum where the stone is located, and feel for the stone in that part; do not move her foot above or below the stone, and make the incision small initially; then insert the probe into the incision, if you sense the stone enlarge the wound until the stone can come out freely, and know that there are many types of stones: small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those with edges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	know the signs to understand the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood flows, place powdered vitriol at the site and hold it for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work until the stone comes out, and have the instruments I mentioned for extracting stones from people ready to assist you in your work; and if the blood flows again, and this is from the artery that was cut, place powder of tents and bendelz on the site and do not repeat cutting there, and leave the stone and do not extract it, as the patient might die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the swelling subsides, then return to your work, until the stone is expelled.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aqueous retention is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white material, which comes from the kidney and contains the egg; it is called "material," and sometimes it is properly within the membrane of the egg, so one thinks that it is another egg; and this is the skin of the bladder between the white material we have mentioned; and this does not happen unless there is a pouch.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this aqueous retention is due to weakness that affects the bladder, and this material spreads out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: where its color declines to yellow, or it is without red, or black, or clear white, and these things happen more; and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is in the whitish fluid that we have mentioned, then the abscesses are recondite, like an egg shape, and do not appear, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper tissue, then the abscesses are recondite with part of an egg, and because of this people think it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the whitish fluid, one can feel it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, examine thoroughly as described above, for its form has been mentioned before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what follows the introduction, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, the patient must be positioned as much as possible and according to the fullness of his body; then place him on his back upon something slightly elevated, and put many cloths under him; then he sits on his left side, and instruct the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the instrument along one of the two ribs near the groin area; then take the scalpel lightly, and cut through the skin in a straight line from the upper part down to just above the joint, making sure the incision is perfectly straight until you reach the white surface, and peel it off gently as much as possible; then pierce the white layer full of fluid with one wide opening, and drain all the fluid out, and then apply your forceps, and lift the white layer upward; do not touch the groin area itself, but only the white layer; cut through everything in pieces carefully and meticulously so that if you do not cut it properly, the fluid will return; if the membrane jumps during your work, reposition it to its place once you have completed the operation on the white layer; then bring together the two sides of the groin area into one seam, and treat it like other wounds until it heals.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to tie the veins that are suspensory, fearing the discharge of blood; then cut the cyst entirely suspensory, and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the swelling is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut the other part as you did the first equally, then dry off the blood, and place on the wound wool soaked in rose oil; and put another layer of wool soaked in wine and oil over it, and place cloths doubled over them, and bind all together according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and wrap them with linen strips according to this appearance and sew them together at the waist of the breeches, one going under the buttocks up to the back, and the other at the thigh part; and both ends cover the two angles, and secure it all around in a loop on the belt; and sometimes this branch is treated with cautery instead of iron cutting, and that means you take a thin knife-shaped cautery, cut through the skin over the swelling, and heat it as we have said, so that the white pus-containing surface is exposed; then take the cautery according to this form, pierce that pus surface with hooks, and scrape with this hot thin cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And cut in all ways that you can, until everything is clear; and ensure that the fire does not touch the eye; and know that this work is safer; and move with caution to prevent blood loss, and handle the procedures carefully; and if anything opposes you, whether it be an abscess or bleeding or something else, then treat what opposes you according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not wish to wait for this procedure due to its horror, then administer puncture as I tell you, and when you are certain by the signs we have mentioned that aqueous fluid is there, make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess from below across the entire span of the swelling, making the incision along the length of the body; ensure that the openings are wide enough for all the fluid to flow out freely; place cotton over the area and secure it, allowing the remaining fluid to drain; treat the wound until it heals; if a white cloth does not allow the fluid to exit from the mouth of the wound, then insert a feather or instrument used for treating edema as described earlier; expand the cavity around the wound, and know that the fluid will return after about six months or so, and when it reassembles as previously mentioned, thus the patient will live their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this branch there is fear in many cases, for which it seems better to leave it untouched; and I will tell you about the work and similar cases of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses occur in the body, especially in the testicles; and this is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is known to be due to sour and acute superfluity spread in the testicles, or from impact; and the color of the abscess corresponds to the color of the skin; and there is no pain, and it is a severe abscess; and sometimes an abscess may be frightful and stony, with a purple color, and at times it comes from a vein blockage or swelling.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is due to an artery, it is known by the hot disposition of the abscess when you press it with your fingers; and you must not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	One who is affected by a swelling of the vein is recognized by its appearance and the sensation when touched with your fingers, and one can properly treat this condition as well as others; cut open the groin area, then place the egg above it, and draw out the white substance therefrom, and release the suspensory from all parts around the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already hardened with these new tissues, then you must draw out the egg and cut it open; and if it is adhered to the tissue or within the vessels, then you must release all of that area and cut it cleanly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is at the back, then it must be cut entirely, and remove the eye, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is complete, apply the wound with moist wool in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a covering similar to the scrotum, with softening of the testicles, and the patient suffers greatly when it moves; and the treatment for this disease is as difficult and fearful as the previous one, yet we will tell you about its work according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you seat the patient on a raised chair, then place the suspensory of the testicles down to your hands, covering all the vessels which are near the penis, and hold them firmly, and stretch them forcefully; then cut with a wide sharp spatula across the vessels until they are uncovered, and then scrape from each side as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in temples; then insert a needle where there is double thread, and tie it at the first place where the vein comes, and tie it again to the other end; then cut straight through the middle according to the length of the body, and drain out the corrupt moisture; then cure the wound as with others when bandaging, so that some vessels do not fall off which nourish one of the testicles; for by this no harm comes, and if all the vessels come down, it is necessary to draw the testicles up to all the vessels; so that the testicle does not lose its nourishment due to the cutting of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot be assisted.
de la routure dou syfac	of the fracture of the cheekbone
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrence of this rupture is by the section that comes from the cheekbone, or the extension over the abdomen in the area of the groins, because the intestines descend from that fracture to one of the thighs; and this fracture is either in the cheekbone itself, or due to its extension, and these two manners come from many causes: such as impact, jumping, carrying, lifting heavy loads, and similar things; and the signs when it is an extension of the cheekbone are that they occur little by little over a long period and do not happen suddenly; and the abscesses are equal up to the bottom, because the cheekbone presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs when it is a section of the cheekbone are that they cause sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear differently, near the skin, because of the exit of the intestines and the body's reaction to the absence of the cheekbone.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines descend with the hernia, and are retained inside, causing great pain for the patient, especially when they are constricted.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments there is fear, because of which it is necessary to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the work is that you instruct the patient to push back the intestines with his hand into the wound if they can be retracted; then place a bandage over his neck between your hands, lift the thighs; then stretch out the abdomen above it, and peel all the skin from the groin longwise; then cut inside the flaps of the waist according to what you need to open the wound, and make them such that the testicles may protrude;
