then peel off the fatty tissue beneath the skin of the groin until the tough white fat is exposed on all sides; then insert your index finger into that which surrounds the testicle, between the white fat below the skin of the scrotum and the second layer of fat, and separate what is behind the testicle from the second layer; then move it with your right hand inside the abdomen, and stretch out the tough white fat to your left hand, and lift the testicles up along the waist; and instruct the assistant to raise the testicles upwards, and undo that which was tied behind the bandage; and ask if there is any intestine wrapped around the tough white fat, and if you find anything, remove it from the belly below; then take a needle with I thick thread made of X threads, and insert it into the back part of the fat layer, after the skin of the scrotum; behind the waist, then cut off the ends of the threads until there are IV threads left; then arrange them one over another in the form of a cross, and tie up the fatty tissue we mentioned which is beneath the scrotal skin with a strong cord from two sides; then wrap around the threads of the cords tightly on both sides so that no vessels that nourish them can enter inside, lest an abscess arise; and place back the bandage according to the first long bandage by II fingers beyond it; and after these two bandages leave uncovered the fatty tissue which is beneath the scrotum for one finger's width; then cover all else around as the testicle carries roundness; then cut off in the part below the skin of the scrotum until there is no more unclean matter or pus left, as we have said previously; then apply moistened linen soaked in oil to the wounds, and place on it the bandage we mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white membrane we have mentioned is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of blood leakage.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and let the ligament fall freely on its own; and if it delays in falling, soak it with hot water, and place what we have mentioned until it falls; then treat the wound with another method until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I have never seen anyone dare to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done like the condition affecting the intestines, in such a way that you bind the vessels, above the navel lightly on the back; then cut into them, and treat the abscess as we have described, until the vessels discharge; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin area, as we have said, and the place is apparent; and no part of the intestines descends to the thighs, but if they do descend, it is serious and persistent; and even so, if it remains too long at this point, the wound or the hernia will grow worse until the intestines descend; and this happens due to the extension of the hernia that is in the groin area, as we have said, because it extends then softens and swells up and becomes apparent; and the treatment for this is through cautery, as we previously mentioned; and sometimes it is treated with a blade in this manner: the patient lies on their back between your hands, then cut around the swollen part of the hernia according to its size, about three fingers wide; then extract the sac that is under the skin as follows, then take the needle and place it over the apparent part of the sac; press firmly against the belly, then sew the two apparent parts of the sac over the top of the needle together; then remove the tip of the needle without cutting into the sac or extending the egg or anything else, as I have told you in the treatment for the intestines becoming entangled; then treat it according to how one treats wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, then anesthetize and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The swelling is constrained, and there is no appearance in the rupture, and the cauterization is soft in this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the genitals
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	The skin of the genitals is often softened in some men because the tissues inside are softened and appear milky; and when one wishes to treat it, make the patient lie on his back, and cut the soft skin over the natural skin; then join the two lips with a seam, and if you wish, sew off the excess soft skin at three or four seams firmly; then cut between the seams, and treat it as other wounds until it is healed, and remove the stitches.
dou chastrement	of the discipline
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You know that castration is condemned in our law, and for that reason I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; but it is necessary for two reasons: the first is so that a physician knows how to respond when asked about it, and knows its treatment; and the second, because we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that castration is performed in two ways: either by traction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method we perform by traction, we have the animal sit in hot water until the testicles become softened and droop; then hold them with your hand until they are retracted and you no longer feel their weight.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the castration of animals: you should anesthetize the animal, and press the skin over the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory bandage, and cut each testicle in one stroke after you have properly skinned them; and leave some soft fat and the fine fat that is on the vessels; and this method of castration is gentler than that done by attraction, because sometimes with attraction some part of the testicles remains, causing the animal to desire lust; then treat the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	Regarding hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermafrodite exists in two ways among men: one is that between the two testicles it has the form of a woman's genitalia, with hair, and sometimes urination occurs there.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other method is for women, and place on the navel as with a rod and two eggs.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for a man and a woman is that you cut the adhering tissues all around, and treat them as other wounds; in the second method, for men whose urine sprays on the skin of the genitals, there is no specific treatment.
de la tentigene	of the examination
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a tissue adhering to the natural part, so that it appears too large and unsightly; some women have it as large as a hand, and this is how it is treated.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should stain the excess of the tentigene with your hand or fingernails and cut it lightly; do not go too deep so that no blood comes out, then treat it as you would other wounds until it is healed; and for another part that grows at the mouth of the vagina, remove it, and sometimes it may bleed, and resembles a horn, hence they called it "horn disease" by the ancients.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you treat it as we have said about tension, and care for it until it is healed.
de erratique	erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is erratic when the nature of a woman's body is not known, or when the passage is small; and it is natural by birth, or caused by illness that comes upon her; or due to added flesh, or thick or thin tissue, and is formed in the uterus, or in the sides, or inside, or wherever it may be; and prevents conception, childbirth, and perhaps having periods; and the knowledge of this is known through examination.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If constipation is close at hand, either use two fingers or the right [finger].
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If the wound is subtle and it is close to two leaves, hurry and treat thus: place your two fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then stretch the two leaves firmly, so that the subtle syfac (wound) lies flat over the swelling; then take linen, moisten it in oil, and place it on the site; then have the woman lie face down each day, so that she may not stick together.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the wound is hard and thick, then you should cut it with a scalpel resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of flesh grown, suspend it at the olecranon and cut it open; and have medicines that constrict blood flow, such as hawthorn berries, dragon's blood, frankincense, mixed with plenty of egg whites; then apply a bandage to prevent the wound from closing; and thus keep it long-term, and treat it with a dry linen dressing; then continue treatment until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when flesh becomes diseased in a wound, it should be cut according to this method, except for embedded abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For in the embedded abscess that is in the wound, one should not cut it open.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without proper treatment usually become chronic; and when hemorrhoids are old they turn hard. And we have already described their appearances and signs in the division, and I will say here those that can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that when hemorrhoids and hard lumps are firmly fixed in the wound and do not yield to touch, they cannot be cured by cautery.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who have the mouth of the ulcer, which can be felt, are those who can be treated by curettage.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you must place the woman in a cold house, then use tongs to lift the altarulum and cut it at its roots, then apply powder medicines that constrict blood, such as oak bark and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bind her feet against the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; if bleeding continues, have her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate peel, gall, and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil to make a paste, and apply this poultice to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if the bleeding stops, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, if you apply cupping to the back and breasts without injuring them; then take flax, and mix it in juice of plantain or agrimony with old wine, and apply it to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red and resembles a hard head, so it must be cut as I have said about the thulul; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	for abscesses of the flesh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the flesh, such as canker sores and stone abscesses and herpes and ulcerations and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary for me to speak in this treatise of the hot abscess that comes in the armpit, which is not one of those that are caught by food; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look to see if the abscess is hard at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hurry to pierce it, but let the abscess die down until the pain is eased; and then have the patient sit on a chair, and give him two small stools upon which he may recline, and support his back and draw together his legs behind the thigh; and let his thighs be spread apart, and place his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a good cloth; then hand over to him towards the right side, and there administer the instrument used for treating the armpit abscess, of which the form follows hereafter; and it is necessary that when you wish to administer this instrument within, you should insert the tip first to know the depth of the armpit, so that what enters into the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the armpit with cloths, so that the instrument does not cause discomfort; and you must place the cone of the instrument at the top, and have him hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is open, and it is cut by hand gently, then it must be cut at the top, at the spatumile site; and when the pus is emptied, then you must place in the wound moistened cloths in rose oil or in green oil of violets; and put the cloth over the wound in the middle of the poultice, and put on the outside of the poultice clean wool moistened in water or mallows cooked; then treat after two days of ointment application as necessary, until it is healed; and sometimes lift the poultice and the wound by enema with water and honey, and then with water or roots of lilies and astragalus long cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is laid on the poultice, then you must avoid heating with iron, but treat it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman press downward, and desire to smell the air: then you know that the child hastens to come forth; at this point you know that this childbirth follows the natural figure, and the passage is under its head, and the second membrane with it; and when you see these signs, you should lightly press her belly so that the child comes out quickly; for when it descends by its head, then the second membrane comes with it, and the child is cleansed of its superfluities through proper cleaning; and those who come forth otherwise do not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes comes upon its feet, and comes forth with the legs or thighs first, or the hands, or it may come out on its belly, or backside, and may be turned around by chance onto its neck, and in other bad positions; thus it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these matters, and wary of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should assist them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out head first by natural means, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, then have her sit on a stool, or where women usually hold; and prepare an oil from fenugreek that has been cooked, and then pour some of this between her two small spatumiles:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the membrane, and scrape it to where the moisture inside comes out; and press the woman's abdomen until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then she must be given a clister of fenugreek mucilage with sesame oil; then have her drink and sneeze on condisi, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands come out first, then you must gently reset them little by little; and if they cannot go back in, place the woman on a seat, and lift her feet up high; then raise the seat off the ground, and support the woman so she does not fall when it is raised; and if the hands still cannot be reset, and the child dies, cut the hands with the knife that is placed here beforehand, extract the child, and reset them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the child upon its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes up on its feet, it is necessary to press them upwards; then turn them little by little until they are even; then take one foot and extend it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it jumps up to the thighs, command it to grasp them, and make it sneeze by tickling; if it jumps further, as God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not go further as we have said, turn it little by little until it is according to its natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will move easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if heat does not come as we have said, take muscil(l)age of aloe, and oil of sesame, and gum melted, and grind all in the mortar; and put the nature of the woman inside and avoid this ointment, then make her sit in warm water up to below the ribs; and when she is moistened below, apply the collar of myrrh and place it underneath, and leave it for an hour; then have her sit on a seat, then cause her to sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly press her abdomen, because the child now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the delivery of the child onto her knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this manner, place your hands gently and slowly under its body; then lift her up by the neck, and let her feet hang down, and lie her on the bed; then bend her arms gently and slowly, and press her hands onto her abdomen, and remove the pillows from below until she is properly positioned downward; if the child does not move, take its feet and maneuver them accordingly, then lift her abdomen upwards, then place your hands underneath again; and deliver the child bit by bit; and instruct the woman to push as soon as the child starts coming out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the birth of the child who comes with one hand hanging down
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary for the physician to return the hand: if it cannot be returned, then make the woman stand and walk; if she cannot walk, then have her lie on the bed with her legs straight; then administer the mixture that I have described; and if she does not give birth, then seat her on a chair, then study how to return the hand; and examine the child according to its natural form, and make her sneeze, and instruct her to hold tightly as the baby comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the birth of the child upon his neck, and with his hands spread out, and his face turned towards his mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the bailiff hold her hand, then turn it little by little, and the water gently; and when it is even, place the natural mixture of earth and oil, as we have said, then command her to move it little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on the chair, and command her to grasp it; and cause her to sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner for the entire second part
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to doing this in the same manner for the entire second part, cut the second part at your nail until the moisture is emptied; and if the child can go up on its face and neck, start cutting from the mouth so that it is not restrained, and move the child; then place the child inside until you have placed it as necessary, and command the woman to grasp it several times: then gently extract.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of the issue of the thighs
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that testicles often develop in pairs, and sometimes three or four may develop; and this is not a strange thing, and it can happen.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	This is a strange thing, and they do not live, except rarely; I know that when they are multiplied, they are separated by the skin that divides them, which is attached to the scrotum; and sometimes they develop as naturally as one would expect, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they emerge severely, treat them as we have said, and let the patient be subtle, and act quickly and gently what she does; and do so as is necessary for their health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the month I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, and all are shaped like children according to the measure of the wise man's age, and it is necessary that the bailiff seizes all of them, because perhaps something similar happens to them; do as is appropriate for them.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of a dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and nothing comes out, and you are forced to work by hand; it is necessary that you know if the woman is healthy and has no accident where she fears death; it is necessary that the woman lie on her back with her legs raised; then the assistant holds two towels, one on each side of her so they do not drag when delivering the child; then wipe the mouth of the month with moist oil mixed with musk of hellebore and fenugreek seeds, then anoint your hands with these oils and mixtures; then gently massage the area, then find a place where it is convenient to insert the hook, and check if the child is prepared to come down headfirst; then fix the hook in its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or in the throat or near the sides, and if the descent is feet-first, then fix it at the knees and sides; you should hold the hook with your right hand, place the curve between your two fingers of the left hand, gently press it into her body, and insert the hook at any of these places until something comes out empty; this is the form of the hook:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert against the other lancet, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is even; and then stretch them evenly by moving from one side to the other, to allow the blood to flow out, and let the lancets have teeth to hold the blood, as shown in this figure:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if any part remains, anoint the edge with some of his oil, and insert it into that part, and draw out the other part; and if anything remains, place this lancet higher up, and do so until everything comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and he cannot bring it back for grasping, you must wrap around the finger until it completely emerges; then cut at the joint of the palm or with a knife, and do the same for the other hand and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is narrow at the exit, where there may be an acute assembly in the head, then you must insert a spatumile between your two fingers, cut open the head, and extract the fluid; or shave it with the instrument called "almidach," whose form comes with the instruments in the chapter that follows this one; and similarly do so if the child has a large natural head; and then pull out the bones with forceps, and if the head jumps forward and tightens on the muscles, cut them as far as the moisture is at the exit of the passage; and if it cannot come out, then cut it piece by piece until you can reach it; and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then you must pierce it so that the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the adjustment to the mouth of the socket is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is tight in the abdomen or breast, then you must stretch it with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and cut the abdomen or breast until the moisture inside flows out; and if another member is removed and the head remains, he should put his hand firmly into the socket, and pull it to the mouth of the socket; then insert one finger or two, and pull them forcefully; and if the mouth of the socket is narrowed due to a hot abscess that has come there, then you must not work on it, but rather treat with moist and fatty substances; and the treatment should be plasters, and also use liquids that soften and moisten.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can make it even, then treat it as we have said about the living child; and if one has no power over it, then cut it up in pieces, and leave nothing of the second skin.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, treat it as we have said about large abscesses that come with swelling; and if bleeding occurs, apply cold water to constrict it, and then use other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whom the fetus in her womb had died, then another was conceived upon it, and that one also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, she developed an abscess in her throat, and it swelled so much that it burst, and began to severely decay.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I pondered for a long time, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a plaster with strong adhesive properties, and out of it came a bone, and after several days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly, for there are no bones in the abdomen.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a deceased child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and extracted many bones, until the woman was at a much better point; and I treated the woman for a long time in this manner, and she would occasionally discharge some fluid from the area; and I recall this chapter only because when masters encounter an unusual thing, they should seek to understand it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the joint to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here follows the form of the binder, which is used according to the books; and for two turns at the two shoulders of the two sides.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle than the binder, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the shaft should be two fingers wide, and the margin of the wood one finger thick, and a length of one palm and a half; and between the two sides there should be two fittings of this same wood, which are firmly set in each side, about half a palm long or a bit more; and these two fittings are placed in the mouth of the joint to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made from ebony wood or boxwood according to the resemblance of pincers; and have at each end two attachments, as you see, one palm long, and two fingers wide; then when you wish to open the mouth with the instrument, make the woman sit on a bed, her feet hanging down and her legs spread apart, then insert the two attachments together into the mouth, and hold the head of the instrument under between her thighs; then work your hand along the entire instrument as you did with the pincers equally, according to the quantity that you wish to open the mouth of the patient, until it opens as much as she desires.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all designed at the top, and their forms vary; and when the doctors have them prepared, they work more swiftly, and are more effective for people according to their quantities.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument because you have not prepared it, for their needs are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze by suggestion, and press your hands over her mouth and nose; if she jumps because of this, so much the better.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot and make a hole in its cover, and place herbs that can open the mouth of the woman, such as calamus, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia lignea, and centaury; all these herbs or some of them should be boiled in water over the fire; then put one end of a tube into the pot hole, and the other end in the woman's mouth, and hold it tightly so that the steam enters her; then make her sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	The second joint moves quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and does not move as expected, instruct the patient to moisten her left hand in linseed oil or muscillaginous of althea, and then place it over the area naturally, and seek the second joint; and when she has found it, take it and extend it little by little straightly, so that the obstruction does not fall out during extraction; but it must be moved gently to the right and left, and then pulled; thus it will come out and release.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the opening of the obstruction is tight, we have said the cure to sneeze and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not move from any of what we have said, be careful that you do not force it out; but it must be that which is at the opening of the obstruction, tie it to the woman's thigh, then administer a four-part ointment enema; this will purge and reset it, and it will come out; but nonetheless, when she purges if there comes an unpleasant odor to her stomach and head, and bleeds the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, appropriate fumigations are necessary for them: some of the ancients have tested fumigation with cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain her flowers and menstrual cycle is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is made of glass resembling a tube, and place the fine end inside the body, and the wider ends over the fire; and let the fumigation be above the coals, and continue until it is spent, and then start another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, but instead it is sealed with a fine sphincter: therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that sphincter at its proper place, and she must not pierce it too sharply, and be careful not to injure it; then apply wool moistened in wine and oil, then treat it with ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will stay in place, insert a lead tube into the hole, and leave it there for several days, and remove it when the patient wishes to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this obstruction comes from the sudden closure of a wound or an abscess; it is necessary to cut open that closure: it should be treated as we have said about the lead tube.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from inside the anus are nodations, and those that come near or between the two parts may have one fistula or more; and when these nodations are old, they work, and still contain moisture like white or fine pus, and sometimes these fistulas are perforating; and they are recognized by what comes out during defecation or flatulence when the patient passes gas, and perhaps a worm is expelled.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate to the bladder, and up to half of the shaft; and they reach to the joint of the thigh, and to the root of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows whether the fistula penetrates to the fundament, and does not penetrate: and it is that you insert your middle finger into the fundament, and insert a fine needle of silk or iron into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has curvature, insert a probe of fine wax or horsehair until you feel the probe or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no passage for discharge, wind, or pus, as we have said: then you know that it does not penetrate; therefore hurry to treat it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula reaches to the bladder or to the passage of urine, then he urinates through it, and cannot be treated with medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it penetrates to the joint of the thigh, then the swelling reaches that place; if there is no twisting and the pain is around it, then it will become a bone abscess immediately, and medicine or treatment with ointment is useless; and for these penetrating fistulas, there is no cure except labor, and vanity of foolish physicians who intervene in them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case that is not penetrating and is not old, there is hope for healing by iron, as I have experienced, and the patient lies on his back; raise his legs up to his thighs, and incline his thighs towards his belly; then insert a lead tent, or a copper one if it is twisted, until you know where the swelling is.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you should insert your index finger there; if then you sense that the tent has been pierced; and where uncovered between your finger is a surface or flesh, then you know it is perforated; do not work on it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is said that some can be well healed, but this happens rarely; and the aid that one does there, is to heat the cautery finely according to the width of the fistula, as it was mentioned before; and insert it very hot into the fistula, until it reaches near the fundament; and do this two times or three, until you know that the diseased tissues are burned, which resemble a feather quill; and then treat with moist tents in butter, until the new flesh grows back, then treat with ointment to heal and join.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus well, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If that cannot be otherwise for him to be well; and if the fistula enters, but does not penetrate to the root which is at the base, and there is a thick layer of flesh or fat between the root and the fistula, and you see the fistula under this covering of the heart; cut from the beginning of the fistula, then push forward through the fistula, and afterwards apply the cautery until it reaches the head of the fistula; thus the fistula will be relieved and fall off; then clean away the corrupted flesh which looks like a feather of a bird, and leave nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood fails you, and it cuts between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or with astringent medication.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cauteries assemble two good things: that is to say, the healing of these wounds adjusted, and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture; then treat with wet bandages in butter or in crushed substances until the wound exudes pus, and thus the burned flesh heals in the pus; then treat the wound with hot ointments made from hard ingredients, and are the medicines dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up to the base of the tailbone and is distant from the body, place your finger inside it and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between two it is the tissue or flesh where it is close to piercing, there should be no doubt in faith and hope through one of the three methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or cut it to the bottom, or if you can place bandages and treat it as first; do not go too deep that you do not cut into the tissue holding the base, and let evacuation happen naturally; then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will heal, or remove that covering which is near the base after cutting, either with a bandage or another instrument prepared; then clean the infected flesh in the wound as much as possible; then work to restore the wound and keep the fistula away from the base: this will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes there are fistulas in this manner: and when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is at the bottom of the foundation near the skin, take a probe with a pointed end according to this shape:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert the thread in a curve from I to II, and insert the probe along the entire length of the thread into the fistula until it reaches the end.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is perpendicular in the margin of the foundation inside, then remove the thread from that opening, so you place your finger on the foundation; and pull the end of the thread, and bring the two ends together, and hold them tightly to each other, and leave it for one day or two; and tighten it occasionally, until the thread fits between the two tissues and they heal; then treat the wound until it is sealed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, pierce it in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to make an incision too deep for the displacement, and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spinous process where one makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and not so on the other, because one should not cut what one must not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	for hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: those that are inside the anus, like grains of resin, and they can be small or large, and some contain blood, and there may be one or several; others are outside the anus at its base or head; but those that are further out have little moisture, and sometimes a bit of yellow fluid or blood, and their color is like flesh. The treatment for those inside the anus is to instruct the patient to take laxatives until the hemorrhoids protrude, and then they can be grasped by the finger; hurry and hold them with your fingernail, then cut at their roots; if the forceps cannot grasp them because of moisture, use a cloth strip or cotton, or a piece of camel hair; pull out by hand, then cut them, and apply some warm powder used for cauterization; follow the instructions in the chapter on cautery to cauterize them, then treat with other remedies until healed; if the anus cannot protrude, administer a harsh and abrasive enema to cleanse what is inside the anus so that it can come out easily; when the patient is cleansed, if the threads are outside the anus, treatment is easier; grasp them by your fingernail or forceps, cut them, then treat as previously described until healed, and beware of cutting with a knife.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should treat the suturing in this manner: take twisted thread and put it on a needle, then pull the thread from above and pierce the needle from another side, and twist both ends of the thread under the needle, and keep it loose; then tighten the thread firmly, tie the thread, remove the needle, and do so for all others, leaving one to drain excess blood; then place a moist piece of cloth soaked in rose oil or cerate on top as padding, and instruct the patient to rest; and leave it until they have healed, treating them with ointment and other care until they are well.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the dryness of the feces or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is dryness of feces in the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is of no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should cut with the point of a scalpel or your nail through the skin above it without letting it dry; then treat it until it is sufficiently moistened as needed; and if it cannot be moistened, then shave more forcefully than before, until it heals much and becomes flayed; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	with trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A flea is a small crawling appearance on the body, and it moves very quickly; and sometimes one feels cold from it, and it is felt as if dead from trembling, and it spreads throughout the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is that you take a quill from a goose feather or a strong vulture feather, and place this quill over the swelling, so that the circles completely cover the swelling; then turn your hand around the entire quill until you cut all around the swelling, and bury it deep, and remove the swelling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a thread of linen or iron according to this form, and let it be fine underneath and drawn over:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, to hold the threads together and press them. And if you wish, cauterize the swelling as mentioned in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes a purge of silver or horehound is made, or of molten brass or bran; and sometimes these instruments are made small and large according to the needs of those who require them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who treat children and those who are weak and in pain use small instruments.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large purge is as follows, and the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there should be a space where the belly is bound as you see, and the center should be pierced; and on one side it has two holes, and on the other side one hole; and the belly where the medicine is placed should be made from an animal bladder or parchment, and should be perforated all around with small holes, and there should be a space of about half a finger between each hole, then insert a strong thread through these holes in ten twists or so, and tie up the belly like a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread, then administer the enema; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with a gentle enema of oil or honeyed egg yolk, or something similar, then pour it in gently; then press the patient's temples with both hands firmly, until he is fully treated, then remove the enema, and raise the patient’s legs against the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him hold as long as possible; and if he sleeps one whole night straight, there will be greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you administer an enema for a disease of intestinal discharge, and the medicine quickly exits, then repeat it until he is well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the fundament or an abscess, then the enema should be as fine as for a child; and this is the form of the fine enema in which the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about treatments and medicines according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds vary according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are from falling on stones, and cutting with a sword or knife, or spear or staff or arrow, or similar objects; and they are made according to the places on the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or foot, or belly, or liver, and other limbs; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, starting with simple head wounds, because memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is from falling of stones or similar things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound is large, and you fear the rise of a hot abscess: then I do immediately cauterize with cephalic [treatment] if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the cauterization be opposite to the injured part; and keep the patient free from overindulgence in wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to cauterize, then reduce his meat [diet], and let him drink no wine, nor eat any flesh; and put on the wound, if hot abscesses come, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, place on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and has not been exposed to air, powder which I will mention shortly; and if the burn has been exposed to air, then apply some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar ones, and the lips cannot be brought together by tents, then sew them together, as I will describe for belly wounds and sutures.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed bone and hangs by only a small piece, then cut it away; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as brains and cooked wheat, as well as peas, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find putrid flesh in the skin that adheres not to the bone, cut away all the putrefaction and apply a poultice, then treat it; and if there is an artery or vein in the wound that cannot be staunched with medicine, ligate the vessel, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light; it is to put in this powder which adheres as the burn has moved.
