Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way of the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live charcoal three parts, and finely powder them, and apply to the wound, and bind firmly until it adheres well and joins with all its blood; then lie it down well, and leave it without removing, unless it swells; for you do not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one uses charcoal alone when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but the burn has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the burn has moved the wound, especially in summer, do not put this powder on it; but apply some digestible ointments, or poultices made of barley flour with water and honey, until it weeps fluid; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the fracture of a bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you hereafter about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there should be no other treatment than to leave it untreated and not apply anything constricting, for this harms the nerves and causes them to retract; nor should anything cold be applied to the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as hot water infused in sweet water, and rose oil mixed therewith, and copper washed similarly in sweet water, and other minerals according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew and ligature with bandages, then treat it until he is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and infected with pus, then pierce it at its lowest point; and if an artery is cut, causing blood to gush out, then open it, ligate it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine in the throat or the windpipe is severed, through which the flesh passes, then sew the wound on the neck along the trachea, without touching the throat but placing it according to its natural shape; and then bind it tightly, and leave it for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until he is healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then scrape it; and if there are pieces of bone, then remove them entirely if you can, and those you cannot take out, leave until the wound festers, and then expose and dilate its exit; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is an abscess, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, then look to see if there is swelling around the wound: you will know that the wound is mortal; but if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it at first, nor bind it for the blood that does not flow deeply, as this could reach the heart and kill the patient; instead apply a drawing ointment, and bandage it twice a day. If you have no ointment, place old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and let the patient rest on the wound for three days, or four, or more; there will be no cramps, nor trembling, nor strangeness of breath; and when you see good signs, you will know that the wound is safe.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it with tents and other treatments until he is healed; and if she cannot heal him, and you work, then you know that there is an abscess; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, either in front or worse on the back, treat it as you would for someone who is ahead; if it is large, suture it; and if it is small, treat it with powder, and if it is pressed against the bone, and pieces are chipped off, then clean the wound, and draw out foreign objects if they are loose; and if they are not loose, let the wound heal by itself, which will ease the extraction of embedded objects; and judgments for other wounds on other limbs are as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the abdomen is great and medium and small; from the large wound sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines protrude, which causes the insertion of them; and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a smaller wound is worse than a larger one because if you do not immediately replace the intestines, they will retract more tightly when they feel cold, thus causing more problems. For this reason, it is better to handle small wounds, as you can more easily return the intestine to its place compared to other methods; and know that there are four types of abdominal rupture: two common sutures occur in the suturing of the abdomen, and the sutures for other body wounds also have two other specific types; yet all these are more closely related to the suturing of the abdomen, and I will explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestine protrudes, and it is a difficult thing to replace, this can be done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a piece of cloth in hot water alone, or cook it in water with sciant and cypress and spica, and rinse the intestine until the swelling subsides; and sometimes use constricting wine to help reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or decoctions of hellebore and mallows, for this eases entry gradually; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is such that one should not cut unnecessarily unless there is great need; and here is the instrument for making the incision: cut inward along the curvature without coming out, and see here its form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, put them back in their natural place if you have the power, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the back part of the abdomen, you should make the patient lie on his back with his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the front part of the abdomen, raise the head and feet higher than the affected area; and also if the rupture of the abdomen is in one of the two parts, arrange so that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus you should treat large and medium wounds as I say.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds apply what is appropriate, then have a minister who holds the entire rupture with their hand and brings together the edges; this is the common method of suturing. Take one or more needles according to the width of the wound, leaving about an inch from the edge of the wound, and insert a needle with strong thread at that point; pierce both sides of the skin with the two inner parts under the skin until you have pierced it completely, then bring together the four ends and tie them tightly around the needle with double thread on either side. Then continue to join the edges of the wound inch by inch, leaving an inch between each stitch, and insert another needle; bind the thread as you did for the first needle, continuing in this way until the entire wound is sutured. The needles should be medium-sized, neither too fine nor too thick, because very fine needles cut through flesh, while overly thick ones do not fit well: therefore they must be of medium size. They should not be inserted too far from the skin and the flesh, as this can harm the patient before the wound heals; trim the ends of the needles so that they do not hurt the patient when sleeping, and place pieces of cloth or fabric over the needle tips to keep them in place until the wound is healed. This method of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds. A second common method involves bringing together both sides of the skin and both inner parts under the skin with a single medium-sized needle and strong thread; when you have pierced all four ends completely, tie off the needle at the point where you started, as one would sew cloth. Leave about an inch between each stitch; this method is known by people. I myself sutured a wound on someone's belly which was cut with a knife, and the wound was more than a handspan wide, with intestines protruding two handspans in length, located directly on the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to him after it had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound was sealed up until fifteen days, and I treated him, and he was well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was well.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and pierce from the outer part to the inner; when it has pierced the kerchief straight through, hold the head of the thread where you have inserted the needle, and let it pierce again from the inner part to the outer; and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as tailors do with fur, and leave the thread on one side once, and take it up on the other, until the stitching is entirely complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, which Galen describes properly, is as follows: one joins the two parts naturally together, and brings the head of one side to the head of the other side in such a way: insert a needle at the nearest head of the muscle, piercing only that place, leaving the two heads of the suture; then turn the needle and pierce from the outer part to the inner part through the two heads of the muscle; then pierce one and the other from the outer part to the inner part in two other heads of the muscle on the opposite side; and this is the worst method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this and some attest that one should sew the belly with two needles, each having its own thread; and one must insert one needle from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew belts; and note that when the rupture is inside the belly, the suturing is more difficult than for other places on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is like the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as if the flesh had not yet moved, put back the intestines and sew them; then apply healing powder to the flesh; and if the flesh has moved, apply any ointment present until the wound drinks in the treatment; and stitch the wound, and let the edges of the flesh be sealed together; then treat the wound as you would others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, put on old cotton immediately when it starts to drink in pus, and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will affect the principal members, it is necessary to moisten fine wool in warm olive oil or rose oil, and place it around the armpits and below the shoulder blades; and if there is pain or putrefaction in the bowels, which often happens, then give an enema of boiled black wine, especially if the putrefaction reaches the intestines; and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it heals more easily than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is pierced, and this is due to the smallness of its veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the spleen jumps out of the wound, put it back in as you would with the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned black or dark, then tie off the area that is black so no blood can seep through, because there are veins and arteries there; then cut away what is between the ligament, and let both ends hang from the part below the wound to ease its extraction when the spleen falls out, and the wound will close.
de la routure dou boueil	of the fracture of the eye socket
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn, and the wound is small, it can sometimes be repaired in some people, as I saw a man pierced in the belly with a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, from which feces and wind came out; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not stop suturing until he was healed, and the flesh closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it close, I feared that the patient would suffer pain in his abdomen; but he felt no pain, and was in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experienced practitioners said that if there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be treated as follows: take sutures with large heads, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the suture opens its head, place it between the two lips so that they clamp onto it; then cut off the head, and this holds fast so that it cannot come loose, then put another suture in after it in the same manner until the entire wound is closed; and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the head of the intestine becomes inflamed and causes no harm to the patient, one can ligature the intestine with a fine thread that matches the intestine of an animal in this manner: take the tip of this intestinal thread very bare, then twist around it a fine linen thread, then insert the thread into the needle, and sew up the intestine, and tuck it back into place; and this method of stitching is not contrary to faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the main intestines, there is no danger or harm, unless due to subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it begins to discharge, is generally called a "fistula," and especially when it is deep and goes inward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the truth an improper knot hard and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also thin like a feather of a bird; and sometimes it forms clear pus, and other times thick; sometimes little, and other times enough; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, this is none other than by one of the IX causes: namely, because of the smallness of the blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the edges, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the place is putrid, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine used in the cure was not good; or because the corruption is like pestilence; or because the property in the region has late digestion, and late healing, and swells by nature; or there are veins in bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary for me to tell you about the treatment of a fistula which is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You should know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or on the surface, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or in some ribs, or in the spine, or at some joints of the hands or feet; and some affect the main property of a limb, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not reach the places I mentioned, and you trust in the treatment, and you wish to understand it, take a probe made of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, then insert it; and if the fistula is curved, use a fine probe made of lead, because lead can bend around the curvature; and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot properly examine it with probes, then wash it through one of the openings, as moisture will pass from one opening to another, and clean it; then carefully press your hand to determine if there is bone or nerve involved, and feel thoroughly, and ask the patient about the pain they feel when pressing, and where they feel it; once you truly know where it is located, and whether it is far from a joint, nerve, artery, vein, or in any of the places I have mentioned, then cut according to what I said, and remove all the bad tissue inside that is corrupted; and then cure until it heals, and if the fistula is deeply straight, you must cut deeply as much as possible, then place moist probes coated with hot medicine at its deepest part, so that the medicine corrodes any remaining excess deep within; and then apply ointments to heal new flesh until it is healed; and if it does not heal by this method, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone has been corrupted by the fistula, cut it away.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not trouble the principal limbs as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then treat it until all the corruption is removed, then heal the flesh with medicinal substances until it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, and returns to its former state, know that you have not yet reached the depth: uncover and search until you are at the bottom, remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healthy, this is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small corrupt bone that you can pull with forceps, then extract it with the appropriate instrument, and if there are many bones, remove them all, do not leave even one; and if the moisture impedes you, and there is no error or fear, cut through both flesh and bone, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them at once, place on the wound something that promotes putrefaction, and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then they will have more easily the bones; and if it is a large bone, such as of leg or thigh, then remove only the corruption until all blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is much part of the corrupted tissue, reaching to the marrow of the bone; you must sew and cut out everything up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something that entered his body, so the substances reached his leg and it swelled with a large abscess, but there was no cause to let out pus; however, the physicians, through their foolishness, operated excessively on the abscesses until they opened them up, and much matter came out, turning into a fistula, and many openings appeared that all discharged fluid and moisture from his body. Many doctors treated him for two years without any skilled hands in the art, until I was called to see him; I saw his leg and the medicines being used to treat him, as well as what was coming out of the openings into his large body; his young man's skin turned red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that they came together from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, which was corrupted and perforated; the corruption reached as far as the inner bone. I treated what appeared to be the corrupted bone, thinking there would be no other corruption besides that which I removed. Then I began to treat the wound with internal medicines for a long time, but it could not heal. So I started again, cut into the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone; I treated it, then removed it, and tried to close the place; but I could not do so until I had cut around one palm's width of the bone down to its marrow, then treated it with medicines. It healed quickly and closed up, except for the weakness of the patient who could not endure further treatment and my fear of death for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often there was blood evacuation, but he remained entirely healthy, and in the place of the bone grew hard flesh, and he had good disposition without any harm or contrary effect whether going or coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated as follows: take some linen, and pull it at the end of the visible bone, and have someone else hold it up; then place a thicker piece of woolen cloth over the skin covering the bone, and stretch the end so that you can draw the corrupted flesh inward, and expose the skin where you wish to treat, making sure the dressing does not harm the skin; put an ember or tablet under the bone to help cut away the corrupted flesh; and continue treating until one can see and feel no more corruption, and repeat as necessary.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and it does not appear clearly, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it, then uncover the flesh entirely; then place a coal underneath, and then tie silk from one side to the other over the corruption, and let the thread be as long as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut off the corrupted joint, and tie the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is between two joints, there is no remedy but cutting; and if the corruption is in the knuckle of the hand or foot, it is very strong that thing, but nevertheless you must inquire about this corruption, how it appears to you; and purify it in all ways that you can, but let the veins or nerves not oppose you; and know that the instruments for cutting these bones are many, according to the setting of the bone and its appearance, and their thickness and fineness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument suitable for each kind of work; and know that the task will show you the tool you need, according to the knowledge of this art and the testimony of the ways of diseases; therefore consider the tool you need according to what is required.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head may rot from within or outwardly; and when you have treated that corruption with medicinal care, and it does not improve, then it is necessary to amputate the limb up to where the corruption begins, so that the patient escapes death by this means, or by the greater evil of losing the limb; and the sign is that the limb turns black, as if burned by fire, and rots after turning black, for the corruption spreads from limb to limb and reaches throughout the body; therefore, hasten to amputate, and if it is due to being struck by venomous beasts, such as a sea scorpion or viper and similar creatures, if the corruption is at the top of the head, then amputate, and give no time for it to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, cover at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cut with a knife; and if it passes the knife, death is certain, and no remedy exists beyond the power of its strength; and do the same when the corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, cover after the other joint; and if it reaches the foot, cover the entire foot; and if it ascends into the leg, cover at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no remedy but to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or covering the limb is that you bind above and below, and stretch one minister the lower cord, and another minister the upper cord, and cut apart the flesh between the two cords at one span wide, until the bone is uncovered; then cut or cover, and place a piece of linen on each side so that the cutting does not touch healthy skin and cause other injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you work, cauterize the area quickly or apply some constricting powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the injured limb with an appropriate bandage and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in a certain instance: he had a black spot that seemed like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his foot’s toe, spreading over the entire foot; when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to amputate the foot, and was healed; and after some time, the corruption returned to his hand's thumb, and he came to me, and I applied counter-irritants after cleansing his body, but could not stop the corrosion; and he decided that I should cut off his hand, which I did not want to do because I had hope of repelling the matter; and also feared that if I cut his hand, he would die, since his constitution was weak; and in despair, he returned home and hastened to amputate his hand himself, and was healed; and I have only told this for others who may face a similar situation.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess appears in the flesh and remains so long that it gathers a great amount of pus; then it bursts and drains, leaving the flesh like a vessel; and the skin above is as delicate as fine cloth, and does not extend to the bone or nerve, and such diseases are called "sain," and are not called "fistula"; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone thoroughly, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you cut around that skin entirely, and similarly when it is delicate, like fine cloth; and it does not matter for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you trust that the skin will contract and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with a clister as follows: check if the breast is swollen, and the pus coming from it has an unpleasant odor, then administer a clister of Egyptian medicine made like this: take aloes, oil, and litharge in equal parts, put them in a container over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take according to your need, mix with water and honey or vinegar, and administer it into the breast while plugging the opening; leave the medicine inside for two hours, then expel it by pressing gently; do this several times until the breast is clean and the foulness removed; sometimes you clisterize with ash water when this medicine is not available, which involves pouring water over vine wood ashes, straining it, and administering it until you know that the breast is thoroughly cleaned; if the patient cannot tolerate either this medicine or the ash water, then administer a clister of water mixed with honey or wine with a little litharge ground in; or use a clister of honey and wine blended together, where honey has the property to cleanse and wash, while wine aids in healing; once you have done this and trust that the breast is clean, clisterize it with something that promotes flesh growth, which can be made by mixing an ointment diafinitum with rose oil and vinegar or wine; or use other medicines and ointments whose properties I mentioned when discussing ointments; if the opening of the breast is small and the tube for the clister cannot enter, widen it a little with iron, place a tent filled with Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is wide enough; if the wound is too large, then suture only the area where the clister can enter, and if the pus-draining opening is higher up, cut below that point.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the boil is deep, it does not allow flesh to grow within; and if you cannot cut under the breast as you wish, prepare in such a way that the pus runs to the lowest place there can be, for when the boil is deep, it does not allow flesh to grow within. If you cannot cut under the breast as you wish, prepare in such a manner: that the pus runs down gently and leave nothing of the boil behind; then take consolidating medicines to put on the healthy part, and lay over it a cloth made of flax covering all the healthy area; then cut at forceful places the hole of the breast a little wider than the first, place ointment under another cloth according to the size of the hole, and set it over the hole in the health to ease the boil, and remove not the large cloth outside until after many days once; and that which is over the hole of the breast, remove often to take out the pus, and examine what runs from the boil whether it is venom or little or enough, or digestible, or indigestible; and watch if the patient feels pain in the place or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been laid out in such a manner and you see the nature that jumps over the hole of health, know then that the breast is healing already, and the sick one approaches health; and then loosen it in the morning, on the third day, and when you loosen the wound, change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the stomach throws up undigested food after many days, know that the stomach does not settle.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle symptoms appear after a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are those to whom meat heals their wounds slowly, and others who do the opposite; and if undigested food rises from the stomach after many days, know that the stomach does not settle; and if digestion is delayed and prolonged, add drying medicines in substance but dry in virtue, such as a diaphoretic ointment, for it contains much vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take a diaphoretic ointment made with rose oil, and rinse it with equal parts old wine; then condense it and use it; and the same is better when thickened, if a diaphoretic ointment is not present, or take myrrh, aloes, and incense, grind them together, and powder over honey while it is on the fire; then glue a piece of cloth to it and place it on the stomach; sometimes administer an aromatic long herb and roots of celestial lily, which are like fine wheat flour and centaury; use simple or compound remedies: grind them into powder, mix with the honey I mentioned, and apply; and if healing is prolonged and not cured by this treatment, then know that corruption has set in deeply and affects the bone, or hard limbs, or ligaments; treat it with the fistula cure as we have described before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarisis is an abscess that arises from beneath the nail of the hand or foot, or occasionally in other fingers; and when it ages and no attention is given to it, a large abscess comes, running and discharging pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and possibly spreading all over it; and corrosion reaches up to the bone, causing putrid pain, and the head of the finger becomes swollen, and the color is livid.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the section, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cut away all the excess that remains from the nail, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great aid if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the flesh, and it begins to hurt, and becomes inflamed, then you must place the edge under the nail that hurts the flesh, and lift it up, and cut away that flesh subtly and gently, and put medicines burning and corrosive upon the rest of the flesh to remove all; then cure with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it out and draw forth, for as long as the corrupted part of the bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see that the tip is corroded, then cut it off from there as was said before, then treat until it heals; and if it is pierced and stuck, and the patient feels great pain, then first must heal it; then cut the nail diagonally with a sharp knife, and be careful not to cut into the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, put something on that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the swelling of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The second joint that is born in the hands of some men is entirely flesh, and sometimes it has bones, and at times there is a nail; and some of them are born at the root of the joint, where the origin is in some places.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born with a knot in the finger do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the finger may sometimes move; the size of the one that is flesh is very small, as follows: measure it from its root by one span.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born at the root of the joint are difficult to treat: be cautious about cutting them.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or should be at the back door, it is necessary that you cut first the flesh roundly until the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable thickness for him, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that comes to both together comes by birth, or by the healing of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut that swelling so that the parts repair according to their natural forms; then place between two cloths or moistened linen in rose oil, so that they do not swell again; or place between two pieces of fine cloth until the area is healed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to either of his two hands with the palm, cut that swelling as it should be done.
des vils	of worms
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are thick and wrapped, full of melancholic superfluities, which occur in many parts of the body; and more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer enemas to him at times, and then treat him with the herb basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is according to two methods: one is that you cut and draw out the black blood; and the other method is that you open the vein and let it bleed completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The treatment by bloodletting is according to this method: first apply a hot water bath to the leg very strongly, until the thick blood becomes thin, then strain the patient's leg from above the thigh down to below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two or three places, each incision being wide, then raise and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one side to the other, as much blood as the strength of the patient can bear; then apply a bandage, and instruct him to abstain from foods that promote black bile; and repeat the evacuation and treatment when the veins are full, and at night it is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The lifting of the vein is done in this manner: raise the patient's leg if there is much hair, then place it in a bath, and wash the leg with hot water until it becomes red and inflamed veins appear; and if you do not have a bath, warm it by fire, and then cut along the length of the vein from the top of the knee to below the ankle; then work the skin with an incision, and strip the vein on each side until it feels hard when touched; and one can see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it appears like a white cord; then lift it under the skin as much as possible, and then gently smooth it out, then cut another place above three fingers' width; then peel the skin over the vein until it feels tough, then raise it to the incision as you did before, and use another hook as you did first; then make another cut or more if necessary, then lift and draw it up to the second cut; then pull out each segment one by one, until it comes out completely, then cut it off; and if you cannot pull and raise it, put a needle along its entire length firmly double, tie and draw it, place an under-skin incision, move your hand from side to side until it is done; beware that it does not break, for if it breaks, it cannot be drawn or lifted, which harms the patient; when you have completely pulled it out, put wet wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound site; cure it until he is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it sharply, but do not cut it off; and pull it out as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the knife used to cut the vein is curved and does not cut, so as not to sever the vessel; it is thickly curved, because if it were fine, it would cut into the vessel, but it should be thick as we have said, and this is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein appears in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry ground with little moisture; and by chance it may appear elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to putrefaction that comes beneath the skin, as it arises within the body like serpents and worms, growing between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there comes a very large inflammation in the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to come out, as if it were the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein is open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of linen one and a half to two fingers wide, and tie it, and let the linen hang down the leg; every time there is a point coming out, wrap it around the linen and tie it. If it is too long, cut off part of it and wrap the remainder, but do not cut at its root until it comes out entirely; for if you cut it, it will enter back into the flesh causing an abscess and corruption in that place, which would cause a bad illness; therefore, treat this vein little by little until there is nothing left on the body. Sometimes this vein when treated is five palms long or ten, and one hand was twenty inches to me from where it comes out for ten palms in length, and when you cut it, you put a reed or tube into it and pierce it completely so that everything comes out; then empty the matter inside and apply medicines against corruption some days, then treat as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein is superficial, especially when it appears at the joint of the foot, or in the foot itself, and there are many perforations through which blood can flow freely; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "bovine illness," because it often occurs in oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body moving up and down, and one can feel it well as it moves from limb to limb, until it breaks through the skin where it goes, causing pain; and it is engendered by putridity of some humors, just as worms, serpents, lice, and ascarids come from the intestines; and there is fear of its malice, because when it travels throughout the body, if it reaches the head, and comes to the eye, perhaps it enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it necessary to cure and drain it, one cannot do so forcefully: therefore you must bind the area above and below with a strong, tight bandage, then cut into it and draw out the pus; and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh and you cannot find it, cauterize the spot with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it can corrode the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the eye, then firmly hold down the eyebrow below it, cut into it, and draw out the pus; and the patient must use purgative medicines to remove bad humors and a diet of non-inflammatory foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to certain limbs, and then it moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, where I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise as quickly as a worm towards the shoulder, faster than anything, like quicksilver when it flows from one place to another; the pain left that spot and lodged in the shoulder, then a little while later spread throughout her body until it reached the other arm; then she told me it was moving rapidly around her body, just as I had observed.
