Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly at how it moved from limb to limb, because I had never seen this disease behave in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had seen many who wished to move pain from one place to another, but I did not wish it, as I saw in the woman; and I thought it was because women have dry bodies, and veins uncovered, and thus this windiness appears constrained; and it does not appear according to this reason for those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and veins hidden.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you wish to treat this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said, lift it up and down quickly, and then incise until that constrained windiness is expelled from its place; and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it with your own eyes, cure it by those who expel winds, such as foul pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows vary according to their forms and the parts of the body where they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of arrows is such that there are those with large points, small points, barbed points, and fixed points; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and when one pierces any limb, it does so in two ways: either piercing a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, spleen, ribs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it pierces any part of these members and the signs of death, which I will tell you next, appear: then you must beware of extracting this arrow, for death often follows in many cases; but when these signs do not appear and the arrow is not deeply embedded, remove it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the brain when an arrow hits and pierces the bone, and bursts the dura mater which is above the brain, are scotoma and numbness and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of tongue, and spasm and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile; and sometimes it comes out without strength from the nostrils, or from the ears; and perhaps speech and voice are lost; and from the wound comes white moisture like pus, and also oozes like flesh water; and if these signs appear to you, then hold off on treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the arrow when it hits the heart are that it is near the left mammary region, and feels as if it were embedded in something hard, not empty; and perhaps the arrow moves like pus, and brings black blood, and comes coldness and cold sweat, and syncope: then you know without doubt that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that pierces the throat is that white foam spouts from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes in the cover of the hip, it is near the small ribs; and throws out great pain and great suffering and sighs; and all the members from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes in the stomach, by chance something of undigested meat may spout from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes in the belly, and feces come out through the intestines, there is no hope for recovery, nor for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes to flow, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and upper arm and spine of the back and forearm and thigh and legs, and limbs similar to these, are safe according to many positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, for that reason do as follows.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow fell into his nasal cavity at the base of the nose: I felt it and drew it out from the other side under the ear fat, and he was safe without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And he drew out an arrow that had struck into the fat of the eye beneath the membrane below, and the arrow was embedded, and only the tip toward the shaft could be reached, and the arrow was large for a Turkish bow, made entirely of light iron without wings; the patient remained healthy, and no ill accidents befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And he drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arab arrow with wings: I seized the barbs, and carefully extracted it, and the Christian remained healthy.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And he drew an arrow from a man who had it embedded in his abdomen, and I thought he would die; and after thirty days had passed, there was no change in his condition; I incised around the arrow, and maneuvered it, and forcefully extracted it, and he suffered no ill effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to treat a man who has an arrow embedded in his back, and the wound is sealed over; and the arrow remains inside him, and he does not change his natural disposition, nor finds harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you wish to treat another man who has an arrow shot into his face, and the wound is sealed over; and he remains without suffering great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And an arrow was lodged in the head of the king's prince, embedded between his ears, and it was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrowhead was entirely buried. I was called for treatment three days after it occurred.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I asked her to do it with great caution, and I felt nothing; and she felt pricking and pain behind her right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I applied a plaster that is both attractive and digestive to prevent swelling; and the area around the arrow appeared swollen.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the plaster for several days, and reopened the wound, and the patient remained in this condition for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose one day; and then he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was open, and I probed it, feeling the tip of the arrow that was lodged in place; then I further opened the wound with this corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow appeared visibly; and after about four months, I stretched the area around the wound so much that I could fit pliers into it and move it back and forth, but it would not come out; then I continued to carefully devise various tools until one day I was able to grasp it with well-made pliers according to what will be described at the end of this chapter, and I extracted the arrow, and closed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physician judges that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored: I then repaired it, and the wound was sealed, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you about the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you do not focus on what I do not say, for books cannot encompass everything; but wise masters compete over great matters, and concerning what is present and lacking, they find new methods, and new instruments, in descending from strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not exit from the members where they are embedded except in two ways: either from the place where they entered, or from another part; and those that come out from where they entered, are penetrating arrows, and sometimes they now come out immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, leave it until the flesh around it is rotten and the exit is clear; and also if it is fixed in the bone, and cannot be removed, leave it thus for some days, and soften each day; then it will come out, and if it does not come out, pierce around with a fine point until the area around it is enlarged, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head and goes to one of the cavities of the brain, and some of the accidents I have mentioned appear to the patient: do not extract it, but leave it for a few days until it is even, because if the arrow reaches there, death will follow.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is embedded only in the bone, and does not reach the surface of the skin, and the patient remains safe for several days without any bad incident, then one should attempt to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, then administer poultices around it, as I told you; then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in a place within the body where it cannot be seen, search throughout the area; and if you can feel it, extract it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or veins around, then cut until the wound is large enough; and extract the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs by which it holds fast, remove the flesh that is embedded from two sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the barbs so that you may pull out the arrow; and be careful not to break the arrow, for you would make extraction more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the area around the site is ripe, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood opposes you, then treat it as we have described in its chapter; and beware of cutting the nerve and vein, and place an instrument so that you may draw out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and position the patient according to how they were when the arrow struck them, for this is the greatest aid there can be, and if you cannot, then place it as the signs direct you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where it appears to leave some mark, or the skin is swollen in such a way that it can be seen or felt clearly: cut above it until the forceps can grasp it, and then extract it; now you must act quickly.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held by the bone, rotate your hand circularly until it enters the bone, then expand the bone, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is there, push it along with all of the shaft; and if the shaft breaks off, and you wish to administer a probe, provide the instrument head so that the point of the arrow enters into the tip of the instrument; and then push firmly, and if the arrow is embedded, push in the instrument at its point to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, it is necessary that you cut away all the flesh around where the wound is, if you can, and then treat the wound as required.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls on the foot or in the belly or bladder or side, and it is near, and you can cut above, do so; but guard against cutting the vein and nerve, then extract, and then sew up the wound if necessary; and treat until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to treat arrows is like the beak of a bird, and see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the piercing needle is also like the quill of a bird, to pierce at the tip of the arrow, as shown here is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the pincers for inserting and grasping is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins from which one can bleed to be cured, sixteen of which are in the head: two beating veins behind the ears, called the 'herbech'; and the two arteries that appear on both temples; and the two veins under each eyelid, called 'aspires'; and the vein across the forehead; and the vein at the top of the nose; and the two jugular veins in the neck; and the two veins above the mouth on the lips, which are called 'augeherich'; and the two veins below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are V in each arm: the first is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and those who practice medicine call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "femoral", and it consists of the cephalic and basilic veins, and those who practice medicine call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is on the right side, and those who practice medicine call it "vein of the abdomen", and it is above the fossa, and this is the one from which one commonly bleeds, which appears manifestly on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salivary vein is the one between the auricular and the ring finger, and it has II branches; and in the leg and on the foot are III veins: the first is behind the curve of the left-side pouch, and the second sophene which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called "nesse", which is at the other side's ankle; and in the other leg are III veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bloodletting from the veins that are behind the ears helps with chronic catarrhs and migraines; and the qualities of the procedure, as I tell you, are that you lay back the patient’s head, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then compress the patient's neck with a bandage so that both veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent on the head: press them then to your palm, and at the spot below your thumb where you feel the pulse, make an incision; then take the lancet and insert it beneath the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire length of the vein, and cut through both skin and vein cleanly two fingers' breadth, and let out as much blood as you wish; then tie it off and bandage, until it is healed; and I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bloodletting from the two arteries that are in the two temples is worth doing for chronic migraine, and persistent headache, and customary ophthalmia with continuous tears in the eyes; and the qualities of the bloodletting are as I say: it is that the patient tightens his neck so that the two veins appear clearly; and feel the pulse under your finger, then cut above; then lift the heart above the vein on top of your finger, and insert the lancet below, and raise the vein up, and cut it, as you have done with the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your necessity; then untie the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then form a bandage tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about their coagulation and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The vein of the forehead is worth as much as the cephalic vein for ancient face diseases and for migraine and redness; and its quality is that the patient strains his neck by twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "digger," here is its form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you wish; then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is secure, sometimes using a wide bandage.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not appropriate for the bandages to be too sharp; and the vein should run diagonally, as the bone is close by, and by chance might break the bandage when it is fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bloodletting from the two veins that are in the two temples helps with the eyes, and for blepharitis, and for redness, and for cataracts in the eye, and for diseases of the face; and the quality of their bloodletting is such that the patient strains his neck by twisting some ligament, as before; then he is bled, and let the incision be straight, a little long of flame a little wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the incision is fine, it might break; then let the blood flow, as much as you need, and then bind with cloth, and tie well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bloodletting from the vein of the nose is good for fever, and for severe headaches, and for diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, especially when it is old; and the quality of this bloodletting is that the patient strains his neck, then pinches his nose with your left hand, and take a fine long incision, and insert it between the lips at the space which is between the two nostrils, because the vein does not show well inside, and the blood will now begin to flow; do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your necessity, then bind it for one night, because it heals very quickly; and this is the form of the incision:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The salve of the two guindages helps in constricting the alaine, and at the beginning of mixing, and for many diseases, and for empetigine, and for corrosions, and herpes, and esthiomenes; and the qualities of the salve are that the patient tightens his neck under one and the other as we have said; and let the master be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair, then bind the vein long somewhat widely, then draw the blood moderately, as much as is necessary; then do likewise in the other vein, then loosen the bandage, and tighten all veins moderately so that the patient does not choke; and leave it until morning when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the salve of the leaves
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The healing of the veins above the lips helps in swelling of the mouth, and decay of gums, and splits of the lips, and nose, and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the healing are to have the patient sit before you, and hold his neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by their blackness and by the small black veins around them: so cut each one, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, cut the largest of each side, and do likewise for the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	From the sickness draw out the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The treatment of the veins that are under the tongue is followed by the treatment of the cephalic vein, which is at the constriction of the throat, and for eye diseases, and for mouth ailments; and the quality of the treatment is such that the patient urinates between your hands facing the sun, and you lift the tongue, and look underneath on each side for a black vein: treat then one and the other, and do not go too deep, for arteries lie below.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the arm that are commonly treated are treated in two ways: either by piercing with a broad flame-like needle, or with an olive-shaped fine one like cutting knives, and it is called "anesil"; and they are wide and fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the minor flame is much renowned, and it is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to use for opening veins that are full of thick visible blood, and which contain thick and turbid blood; and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is finer in shape, and is used to treat fine veins, where there is fine yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps in diseases that affect the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen; and it is necessary for the physician to bleed wisely, and to be careful not to cut the artery that lies beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and bleeding occurs, it must be stopped, as I have said; and it should not be cauterizing the flame but cutting as previously instructed.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not appear clearly, then you must remove it and replace it with another; or take some of its parts, or expose the vein in its place: it appears clearly; and cut with a flame as previously instructed.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to determine the location of the incision, then it is necessary for you to extend the arm, touch the area until you find the pulse; then mark the exact location, and then bind the arm, and cut into the vein with a flame as previously instructed; and be careful not to injure the artery when you see the area swollen, because that is from the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it rising up like a child’s urine, and the blood is red and fine, know that this is arterial blood: hurry then, and place your hand lengthwise, then remove your hand if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; and be afraid, and do not move the patient until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding does not stop, and you are in a bind, and no medicine is present, then cut the artery if it appears, for its head retreats; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take the bark of fig tree, and cut it, and take one of the halves and bind it on well until the other day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, then treat it as we have said, with powders that stop blood; and the stopping of the bleeding is not difficult in many conditions for the small area of the wound, and the strength of the bandage of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The incision of the vein in the middle helps to draw blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the surgeon must cut around the nerve that lies beneath, and if he cuts too deeply and finds the nerve, it swells and the patient suffers great pain, and perhaps cannot be healed; this nerve often appears, but if it does not appear in some people due to its subtlety, then you should heal it with a blunt instrument; and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make the incision along its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The incision of the cephalic vein helps to draw blood from the head and aids the eyes; it is necessary to cut along the olive or myrtle vein, as this is the safest of all veins, because there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, one must choose the gentlest spot, and it does no harm if it is not done correctly the first time, and one can retry; and sometimes the area swells when it is done for some people the first time, but it causes no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the salve is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bleeding is that it should only be done to preserve health and to avoid future illnesses; and one must bleed in one of the three veins which are at the site: namely, cephalic, facial, and basilic; and it should be done early in the morning after fasting, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and it should be done on the first or third day, two hours or three days later.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The physician who treats diseases has no set hours, but when there is need day or night, at all times and in all seasons; and it is not proper to treat children until they are fourteen years old, nor women carrying a fetus from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	One should not treat the elderly who have surpassed sixty years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wishes to be treated, in whatever manner it may be, they must cleanse their intestines with a gentle enema if there is much retained feces so that the veins do not attract superfluous and harmful substances from the intestines; one does not treat those who are overly full of food, or drunk, whether they are pregnant or not; nor after colic pain, vomiting, diarrhea, excessive sexual activity, labor, staying up late, and other activities draining strength entirely, whether by weapons or body; then purify the humors if the patient is fat, with food and drinks and medicines if you have the power to do so; then enter a bath, unless anything prevents it, to refine the blood; then let the physician bleed from the arm just before midday as we have said; and guard yourself that day against work, worry, lust, and similar things; be relaxed and cheerful; the physician should be higher than the one being treated, and rub the patient's arm two or three times, then tighten the bandage moderately, for if it is too tight, blood cannot flow; then massage the area with your hands until veins swell and can be felt; then moisten the lancet with a little old oil, place the left hand under the vein where you wish to bleed so that the vein does not move upon piercing.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow like cords to the surgeon, and some are full of airiness, so when one applies the flame, it retreats from the flame, and thus cannot open the vein, and in this way one is with such things; and if he works on the vein, the wound is too narrow, for which reason it is necessary that surgeons be cautious about these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is worked on the first time, it is good; if not, then begin again a little below that place quickly, if the area is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the area is swollen and the patient is frightened, leave it for one or two days and do not tie the arm: perhaps a soft abscess will come; nor enter the bath, then begin the bleeding again if it pleases him; and if the opening is small, place the flame directly on that opening quickly, so that the area becomes swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the area swollen, do not start a new incision again, and put some poultice of oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and at this place the poultice is softer than the oil; and thus administer the poultice of oil each time you cut open veins to stop the flow of blood; and the same thing applies to thyme and birch leaves when they are applied to the area; they subtly refine the blood and disperse it when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens many times, especially when it is not incised forcefully except at the time when the vein opening is small, then hurry and place on the area a sponge moistened in warm water and vinegar for a bit, and press it for an hour; and you should do this after the blood has flowed from the vein, and if some black or green remains in the area after several days, it does no harm; and if you wish, put on the area something made of aloes or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, mastic, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an abscess and swelling appear at the base of the thumb: place your hand then on it, and if you find the spot soft under the pressure of the hand, such appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid then placing anything of what we have said, for it may cut into the artery; but apply a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw out the blood from each according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too warm, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And for one who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, make a wider incision, and let the flaps be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed them little and often, and this should be done by cutting crosswise, not lengthwise; and this method of bleeding saves from blood loss and nerve damage, and is worth more than long or wide bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body needs bleeding, give him moistened bread in pomegranate juice; if he is heated, let him take blood three or four times. And if he has a cold constitution, let him eat before bleeding moistened bread in musé syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and sweet-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after losing much blood, it is necessary that he drinks broth of meat, and subtle aromatic syrup, and uses other things which we have said in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed his arm and faint again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he bleeds little by little according to the quantity of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wishes to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, he should bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wishes to bleed from another place, should bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that is already heated, and it causes fever; thus a large quantity must be drawn out, and the passage enlarged until it flows freely; then when you have fulfilled all the conditions for health, place your hand on the pulse as it heals, so death does not occur in its place, which often happens due to negligence of the healer; nor should you press firmly upon it if you wish to release the arm a second time and the passage is closed; nor if curved, extend the arm hastily, for that would be worse; but leave it until it flows freely the second time; or touch with the tip of flame where the blood which has congealed at the opening of the vein issues forth, place upon it a poultice wetted in water, and press lightly upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not bind it, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, do so from the same vein, or from another vein, or from the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is bled in place of the head vein because it is composed appropriately.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of bleeding is that the patient immerses their hand in warm water until it turns red; then bind it moderately so that the vein becomes firm, and bleed now through it, not wide nor long; make the puncture large, and bleed close to the joint of the hand, and if no blood comes out, immerse the hand again in warm water, and let the blood run into the water until you have enough; and if this is done in summer, do not bathe the hand in warm water as it is more commonly done in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than any other veins because there are no arteries or nerves nearby.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The treatment of the right hand vein is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: pull out the vein, and put it in hot water, until the vein swells if one can see it; and if the blood flows sideways, and you cut it completely through, nothing will harm; and do not go too far, because the nerves are underneath entirely bare of flesh, and then put the hand back into hot water, if the blood has congealed in the wound, and none may come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn blood as much as is necessary, apply oil and wax to seal it quickly, and do this for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The treatment of the left hand vein is good for the disease of the spleen, and do it exactly as I have told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sinew of the sophene is effective against all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the thigh, retention of urine, disease of the thighs and legs, old diseases of the calves and legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its sinew is such that the patient should put their foot in hot water, and rub it on the vein until it softens, and apply it above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there are many veins; treat it then where the largest vein is, or at the ankle, as this is much better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you treat it on the foot, be careful of the nerves that are below, and treat it across as when cutting; and let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, place the foot in a bath of hot water, and allow the vein to be thoroughly opened.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the incision fails the first time, start again slightly higher up, for the area is salty; do not fear damaging nerves, as we have said, and so do the same incision on the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the ankle, and its incision relieves hip pain when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the characteristics of its incision are that the patient enters a bath, and compresses above the ankle four digits by twisting, for otherwise the vein will not be seen; and if it appears, then cut it in all ways you can, including across; and it is better that you do not make an incision, as the location is deep, and it reacts strongly to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, heal some part of the one who shows on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and let the blood flow as much as you wish, and then loosen the bandage, and put cotton and bind it; she is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	suctions of cupping therapy
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping instruments are made of horns, or leather, or glass; and cupping is performed according to two methods: one by drawing blood and the other without drawing blood.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping without drawing blood is performed according to two methods: with heat or without heat; and the cupping that involves drawing blood is done in fourteen parts of the body: one on top of the head; another around the neck; two more on either side of the neck; one below the chin; two on each shoulder; two above the kidneys; four on both arms; two on both legs; and two on both ankles. This type of cupping does not draw blood, except from small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken a person as drawing blood from veins would do; and it should not be administered with or without heat in any disease caused by congestion, until all parts of the body are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if due to necessity of illness ventose must be applied, or by habit, we should do it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and throughout all times; for there are those who, when they need ventose, have a heavy head; and there are some who experience bloating and redness on their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and some who see blood droplets in their mouth, and their tongue swells up and bleeds; and there are those who dream, seeing pure blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially in the middle of the month, we instruct them to use ventose after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The massage of the temple helps with headaches that come from the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventosity is in place of the cephalic massage, and those who have a cold constitution or who suffer from catarrh should not use it, as it does them great harm; and therefore old people should not use it, nor those who have cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who become too frequent in this treatment may become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the cupping slightly lower due to the risk of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventosity on the neck is in place of the massage of the head and the basilic area, and therefore it is useful for tightness in the back, and for fissures in the spinal canal, and for tension, and for repletion; and it should be applied gently, because if it holds too firmly, it may cause forgetfulness or distress to the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventosation between the two ribs of the neck is useful for headaches, and for optic nerve disorders and migraines, and for choking, and for pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is located at the site of the basilica's treatment; and you must instruct the healer to press his hand when applying, that he does not cut the artery, and that there be no bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The ventosation below the chin is useful for mouth diseases, and for gum infections, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is located at the place of treatment between the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventosation of the shoulders is useful for diseases that come from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The venesection of the arm veins is worth as much as that of three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the surgeon not to cut too deeply, for the area is bare of flesh, and lies near nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping on the rump is equivalent to hemorrhoids of the anus, and for diseases below it; it should be large and made of brass because it requires strong suction; if it were delicate, it might break, and thus cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping on the legs is very effective, as it draws blood from the entire body and is beneficial for chronic pains in the thighs, and of the bladder, and alleviates swellings; and they are applied at the two thigh joints, and the two ankles, and overall they weaken the body after prolonged use, and cause fainting in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the cupping vessel is to place it first empty, then tempering, and placing it quickly, moving it evenly, and not ceasing from this, until you see the area red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then stop, and replace the cupping vessels, and take care with the condition of the body, for there are those who have tender flesh, and clear pores: it is necessary to strike only once, and make large wounds, and somewhat deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we wish to draw a little blood at a time, we strike only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we lose a lot of blood, we often replenish it; and if the blood is thick, I apply it forcefully, and the ends are such that the veins are pierced suddenly, and for those who have thick skin and hard pores, you should anoint the spots with an appetizing and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, violet oil, or almond oil, or cucumber seed oil; and if it is autumn, cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take marjoram oil, or balsam oil, or anise oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person being treated has tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be applied, but they should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelainflower water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, let them rise from ease, or with myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large excesses should rise from old wine, or water of juice, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not appropriate to bleed with cups before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath one hour or two; and do not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary for him to wash himself when he should be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And be cautious if the person who is bleeding is choleric, and if their blood is too sharp and inflamed; then it is necessary for them to take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce in ease, and similar things; and drink poultices, and meat of castrated animals, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion should take syrup of honey and aromatic wine that is between old and new, and eat boiled peas, and small birds such as sparrows; on the day they will be bled, they should drink more than they eat; and some people should be given triacle or nutmeg before bleeding, or after, to comfort the principal members; and their diet should be subtle, but those who are hot should not drink this.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping vessels that are applied without injuring the skin are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, for podagra, and on the abdomen and buttocks and thighs and hip, because these members cannot bear being cut; it is only done to draw blood from one member to another, as we place them on the breasts when a woman is nursing; to remove viscosity that is in the member, just as we apply cupping vessels to the abdomen and buttocks to reduce swelling; and they relieve pain when there is congestion or stone, removing by their attractive power perhaps the obstruction, or dislodging the stone from its place; and they do this when placed on the liver and spleen if there is retained wind, these cups are administered empty for suction alone; sometimes they are heated together with fire, and at times filled with hot water, or water in which suitable herbs have been boiled, such as in cases of pleurisy.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping vessel administered by fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and on the side there is one small hole, as if to insert a needle, and it should be made of brass, smooth so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle there is a crossbar of brass or iron, for placing a candle holder, and they vary in size according to the diseases and age of those who use them; for the cupping vessels for children are different from those for the elderly, and for thin people than for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.
