And one should place this cupping vessel on the limb thus: take the candle of wax or ointment, and put it inside the cupping vessel across the bar that is in the middle, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping vessel so it does not burn the patient; then place it on the limb, with your two fingers over the hole we mentioned, so when you want to, the vapor goes out and you can remove the cupping vessel; then take the ointment as before, and repeat often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping treatment for pleurisy, which is applied in all cases of fluid accumulation, there is no handle or hole, and it is used only when full of fluid, and is placed on the limb solely; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Cupping glasses are used only on limbs where cups cannot be applied due to their small size, such as the lips and gums, and similar areas; and in exposed flesh areas like hands or feet, and others alike. And when you find cupping glasses that are in clear fluids without any sediment, take them; place one nut in warm water until they become familiar, and have nothing inside; then sterilize with a vein and a cup, rub the limb until it turns red, and apply the cupping glasses; and when they are full and fall off, if this is an area where cups can be applied, do so, as it is much better afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the place on a cushion and then with cold water, very well, and then press it; and if the wound heals too quickly over the blood vessels, moisten the cloth of linen in cold water, and put it on until the blood is stilled; and if the wound is multiplied, put on crushed vitriol or gallnuts, and similar things until it is stilled; or you can place half a pound of peeled beans on it and let them heat up at the spot, which will now stop the bleeding; and if you need more treatment, take other blood vessels.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the blood vessels do not want to take in the treatment, rub the wound with fresh blood, or insert a needle until the blood flows out, and then place them on it, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will heat up; and when you see that they are sweating, sprinkle a little aloes and frankincense powder, or ash, which will now fall off.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is about the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish doctors throw themselves into this chapter without ever having seen any ancient books or read any letters on it; and because of this, science is strange in our land, for I have never found anyone good at it; and I know nothing about it except through the science of ancient books where I have studied extensively to understand the science, and by experience, and by the customs of my life; and I have clearly described in this chapter what is contained within, and have summarized it at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are used as I have done in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the essentials of speech and the chapters where the wise man places his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, torsion, or sprain comes to someone, it is necessary that you hurry to heal the patient from both sides, if nothing prevents you, such as weakness of body, children, or elderly people; or if the weather is not very warm, or too cold; and eat cold things, that is to say cold jellies, and meat of birds and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not overfill yourself with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a hot abscess, nor an effusion of matter in the limb; if the patient returns to his first proper management.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that cause thick nutrition, such as viscosity, like boiled wheat in water, and rice, and head of fish, and feet, and belly of pork, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For such nutrition helps the healing and the broken bones heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the elderly and infirm cannot heal well or join together according to their nature due to the dryness of their limbs, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but it does not matter, reset on the broken bone a thick splint which holds and joins the limb together until it strengthens as it was before; and do not let them lack in their work, and for this one must nourish them with thick meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the hip, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manners of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the marrow, and another in sharpening, like the shaft of a writing quill.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture that is just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each type has its own method and proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory tells in its place; and a bone fracture is known by its being twisted, and clearly apparent by swelling, and sounds when pressed with the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture; but it may well have a twist, or crack, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not right to move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that follow hereafter, and then hold it firmly now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that goes into the bone, and are the two parts disjoined, it must now be set evenly, so that no swelling comes from abscesses; and if hot abscesses come, leave them for some days until the abscess is eased; then set it equal to the movement you can gently and wisely, and know that the restoration of this one is lighter than those where there are pieces; then hold it firmly as required hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone with pieces broken, it is held by two parts, whether hand or foot, or by one hand for smaller members, or by two cords, or by one cord and your hand; set the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the fractured limb are separated, reset all additions in their places as you can, and ensure that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient; and join well the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And you can feel it well in your hand if it seems to you that it is not right: straighten it properly, and do not pull too hard, nor press as those who cause heat and contraction of the limb through their work often do, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is properly set, instruct the patient well not to move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor in turning, nor in any other way; and ensure that the limb is so secure that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels any pain, it is not properly set, and it must be placed in such a condition that it does not feel any pain; and take care that it is positioned correctly so that no curvature occurs when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb depends on what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in size and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and thighs: they should be bandaged with soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as the thigh and leg: it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and firm cloth, for wide strips of cloth encircle the entire large limb, and bind it equally on all sides, so there are no gaps; then tie around small rollers, three or four times according to the limb, and tighten your hand slightly over the whole bandage, then press above the fracture and tighten less, allowing the fracture to move a little away from the pressure; and gradually loosen the binding bit by bit until you cover most of the healthy area, then take another strip and wrap it around again over the fractured area; then press below the fracture moderately, neither too hard nor too lightly, as we have said in the first chapter above; then place linen or cloths between the bandages to make them even, then tie everything with a bandage on top, and then apply your well-made splints if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply a hot poultice that reduces the swelling and leaves it thus for several days; then incise with your lancets, which should be half as wide as a finger, or made of wood used to make clives, or from palm ribs, and they should be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the lancet which one places on the wound be somewhat larger and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as required for the size of the limb, whether small or large; then incise over the lancets just as you did in the first dressing, and tie a thread around them, as you did with the first dressing on the fracture; tighter above, looser below; and it is necessary that the threads be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and should be of soft linen; for if the threads are too thick, as I have mentioned regarding the work of fools who make their dressings from twisted linen cords, which is a great error, because the dressing cannot be even if it is too fine, and it is not appropriate that there be less than two doigts of space between each lancet.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is pierced by the points of the stars after binding them in their sinews, place below them linen plugs or wool fluff so that they do not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the breaker, and the bone is broken, I will describe the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And you should know that it is not appropriate to extract all the broken members' splinters on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it is not appropriate to place splinters outside until after five days or seven, or more according to your judgment of a hot abscess that might follow; and here is the method of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour from the walls of the mill, mix it abundantly with eggs, apply this preparation not too thick nor too thin, and use it. This is the common method of a plaster that restores fractures in various conditions, especially for women and children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to make a plaster that restores fractures, dislocations, and twists: take benzoin and storax and enule and asafoetida and gum arabic and mastic, each X drams; myrrh and aloes, each V drams; aleche IX drams; and make powder, and mix with yolk of egg; if the person's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is well composed, and quickly restores broken bones, and is good for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way to make a plaster that is good for twists: take mastic and visnaga, each X drams; myrrh and aloes, each IX drams; acacia VI drams; Armenian bole X drams, and grind well, and mix with water or yolk of egg, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to make a plaster for joints and bones out of place, and to ease the pain arising, and the use of the bone, and the fracture: take new wool, and boil it in oil, and apply it to the area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not heal, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses and properly relieve pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to make a plaster that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial plantain leaves, and grind them together, then make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make a plaster for the healing of bone fractures and to reduce the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of vervain, chamomile, violets, flour of oats, of each one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix it with moist coriander water, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of making an ointment stronger than the first one, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of vervain, seeds of flax, hawthorn, fenugreek, and savine, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of each one part; and grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that one should not place anything on a broken limb to restore strength except for plaster made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be neither too hard nor too soft.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says that one should place dry and slightly warm things on a broken limb to restore it, such as myrrh, aloes, and incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to make a plaster that is good for injuries and pain: take mutton suet, hair of men's heads, or bird feathers, and sage, in equal parts, and grind them together, and make a plaster with it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little after, and be careful if the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; do not loosen it by hand for several days. And if pain comes to the area, or itching without rest or swelling, hurry, and loosen it, and remove the plaster now; take a light cloth, and sponge of sea water, and dip in water, and lift up the area, until the itching ceases, and the pain subsides; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry flax moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it with a nut, until you are sure there is no hot abscess; and treat the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then resume the fine bandage, and a little plaster, and do not squeeze as tightly as before; and delicately until he is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is red and swollen and painful and has been emptied of everything inside, and you need to apply a poultice and bandage, then restart as you did initially equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if the limb shows none of what we have said, do not dislocate it until after three days or four or five or seven; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, as is seen, until the swelling subsides and the flesh around it thickens; then reset it more firmly than before, and fatten the tissue as I said earlier; and if you see the area dry excessively beyond what is necessary, know that new growth will not come there; pour on warm water each time you dislocate it, every third day, and loosen the ligature a bit; in this way, therefore, prevent new growth from occurring in the limb, and improve quickly what foolish doctors do by resetting it too soon: this is wrong, and such practices are dangerous, and I see nothing else but leaving it alone and treating it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various kinds of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of fractures, and various figures, and the causes are distinct; for there are fractures that are made by the impact of a sword, and the collarbone breaks all the bone up to the suture which is below the bone, as it does in a tree trunk; and for this kind of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, and this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound from these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded impact, or a split from a stone, or falling on a stone, or other similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a perforating fracture, which approaches as far as the membrane beneath the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound in the bone as fine as a hair, and the fracture is small, and for this reason it is called a "hairline" fracture; and if the wound is caused by being hit with a stone, or falling, or similar things, and causes a piece of the bone to go inward, and the place where the hair is resembles how a blacksmith shapes when hammering on his forge; then a stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often to those who have in their head soft bones, such as the skull of a child; and in all these ways of fractures, small pieces are separated like splinters; and I will speak about them at their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the depression on them, and through examination with probes, and by the corrupted flesh that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is known when, after exposing the bone and rubbing it, the fracture appears clearly black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be mindful of any adverse reactions of the patient, and if you see any bad signs, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, fainting, intermittent fever, and the eyes protruding and turning red, along with other similar conditions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming symptoms and hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person comes to you first, and it is in winter, then you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day from the wound so that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then you must hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue under the bone does not become corrupted, and avoid the accidents we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches to the tissue that covers the brain, then you must proceed as follows: take the head of the wounded person and expose the bone in all ways possible, especially around the wound area as much as you can. If bleeding occurs when exposing the bone or if a pus-filled abscess appears, deal with it accordingly by placing moistened bandages soaked in rose oil over the affected area; allow the wound to rest until the abscess is healed and there is no more bleeding; then begin to cut around the bone according to two methods of work: one method involves making precise cuts beforehand.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make the second cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have various cuts of different sizes, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of iron; and work gently so as not to cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and protruding, you must pierce around it, thus administering cuts with chisels, but not so deeply as to penetrate through the skull bone, and it should have a margin or circle above the tip that prevents it from passing beyond the bone; and you need to have several of them, each fitting in its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have chisels for the entire head; and this is the form of the III methods of chisels:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to pierce around the broken bone is that you place one tarer on the bone, and turn it with your two hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then move the tarer a little further away, and do this all around, then cut with incisors the space of the bone which is between the holes, and do this as carefully and lightly as we have said, so that you draw out the bone into your hand, or with some of the tools that you have such as tongs, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the cerebellum.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and extracted it, then you must resurface the rough part of the bone with another instrument similar to an incisor, but it must be sharper and more delicate than the other incisor; and if there remains any small bones or scales, remove them gently with the tools; then treat the wound with dressings and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of work is that which Galen says, who is more skilled; and he praises it greatly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone where the fracture begins to show, so that when you have uncovered this part, you place beneath the head of this knife with a lens-shaped form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is beveled on two sides, so that the cutting edge faces the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet, so that you lightly groove the bone all around, and take great care of the tissue beneath; if it is adhering to the bone, remove it gently, as it can be removed without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate to the skin, and the bone is only cut slightly from above, with small pieces present, then behind that roughness, remove the scales with a fine scraper of which you must have various quantities, in order to treat each place most suitably according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Use larger scrapers first, and then finer ones, and continue doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair cuts and fine fractures, you must treat them according to their condition; and this is something that cannot be answered by one who has not studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the sinus is exposed, you must take a piece of linen according to the size of the wound and soak it in rose oil, then place it over the wound; then take another doubled piece, and soak it in wine and rose oil, placing this on top of the first piece; do this as lightly as possible so as not to burden the sinus, then cover it with another cloth without pressing too hard that only covers the wound; leave it like this for one or two days until the swelling is calmed, then remove it and apply medicines such as lily root, wheat flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; from these substances make a powder and place it over the wound, and subsequently apply cleansing remedies without causing irritation; ensure that the wound remains clean and do not leave any ointment or allow pus to accumulate on the cloth covering the brain tissue, for when pus accumulates there, it can lead to serious complications.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness comes not from the medicine that was applied, which has such virtue, then you should take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix them together, and apply it to the surface; then treat it in ways that are appropriate until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two upper parts of the spine are broken, or only one part, because these are two bones; and the lower one is made of cartilage, and does not break, unless it is forced to bend or twist, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must insert your small probe or needle into the anus, and place that fracture inside according to your index finger, and behind a pouch, until the anus returns to its natural shape; and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the anus, and your probe cannot reach that place, then you must place it equally at the head of a vein slightly thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is in two parts, then do likewise, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after seven or ten days, when the abscess has subsided, then insert into the head of the anus patches of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you insert one on the other side, if there is a fracture; and let the tents be so thick that they fill the passages of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some doctors say that the tents should be moistened with butter, and changed each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think that is good, but they should be moistened with a preparation of oak bark and egg powder, and powdered miller's meal; then leave the tent in place until the bone is hard, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes goose feathers are inserted instead of tents, and if there is inflammation around, they should be used to blow the fracture site, and the patient can breathe through them; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose while you are working on them, apply plaster or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a bit of myrrh.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no abscesses come to it, apply an external plaster made of sesame flour and powdered incense, cooked with a bit of egg white, then place light cotton plugs, but do not tie up the nose; and if the fracture of the nose is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract them using suitable instruments, then sew the wound, and cure it with things that regenerate flesh and seal wounds, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this purpose; and if there are no injuries inside the nose, treat it with tents, and place strips of cloth until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured away and there is no wound to exit, and the fracture is only inside, not split into two pieces, except for cracks within, one can easily recognize it.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, you should place your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left mandible, place your right index finger there, gently insert into the fracture from inside, hold it with the other hand from outside, and make it equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is separated into two parts, you must administer an extension to both sides until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth occurs, or rupture, then pull them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place on the broken mandible cerate, and put on two cloths; and place on the cloth a large stick well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width according to the mandible, and tie it up as much as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then loosen it on the third day and then put back what has changed; and apply a poultice of mill powder with plenty of egg or sesame flour after removing the cerate; and place light wool over the poultice, and if the poultices adhere and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is well; often it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if small abscesses come, then treat them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both a fracture and a wound together, examine whether any piece of the bone has been removed; then carefully remove it with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with flame according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, then sew the wound closed if it is wide, and apply suitable plasters to it, to promote flesh growth until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The collarbone breaks several times in front of the shoulder, and the fracture is according to three manners: where it is broken and disjointed into two parts, there are fragments, and this is the easiest to restore; where there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is such that when the fracture is without a wound, you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the collarbone is broken; and the other stretches the neck towards the affected part; then equalize the fracture with your hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there be no appearance or displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to stretch further, place under the patient's shoulder a round pad of cloth or wool, and make it thick according to your necessity; then extend and lift the collarbone, and hold the pad with your hand so that you can equalize the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the collarbone out due to its position, then the patient should lie supine on their back, and place a medium-sized pillow under the shoulder, and push the shoulder down by the minister, until the bone of the collarbone is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then align the fracture with your hands, and if you find it shattered, then you must split it open; pull apart the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join due to any protrusion, cut it with one of the incisors that you have; but place this instrument under the collarbone to protect the surface.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it resembles a spoon, and is not bristled, and should be as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two edges, as you see, one broad and the other narrow, like the shape of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, sew the wound closed, and if the opening is small and you doubt a hot abscess, pack the wound with cloths and tents according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if pus comes from an abscess, moisten the cloth in rose oil and vinegar and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The treatment of the bone when it is fractured and without incision is that you place on the bone the plaster made from powder from the mill and egg albumen, and put in light dressings; then place a ball under the uninjured buttock if necessary. Take a very wide bandage one palm wide, and lay the double cloth and plaster over the dressings; take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that its ends hang down. Place the stick on the fracture, then roll the bandage around the neck, under both buttocks; tighten each part separately, and when you see that the joint holds the fracture properly, and clearly the stick does not move over the broken bone, observe it every day, and whenever the ties loosen, retighten them. Make the patient lie on his back, and place a small roll under the uninjured buttock to lift the injured one; this will ease the shoulder fracture by raising the shoulder, where you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless an adverse event occurs until twenty days have passed; then reapply the plaster if necessary, keep it tight, and leave it on until he is healed; it takes about twenty-eight days for healing in most people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It rarely happens that the shoulder is broken wide or in the middle, and it can only be felt by touch; then he sets it according to the shape of the fracture and resets it according to its natural form in all ways possible; then put on the place powder from the mill with plenty of egg whites, and light bandages, and lay two cloths over it; then place a wide and fine splint, somewhat wider than the shoulder, and if the end of the splint protrudes at any point along the shoulder, fill that part with linen bandages so that the splint lies evenly; and then bind it tightly all around with a broad strip so that the splint does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and whenever it loosens, tighten it again, and keep the splint in place if it moves out of position, and have the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder will be healed in twenty or twenty-five days, and when this number is completed, release it, and be sure for there is no bone that sets lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes and is outside the chest, they cut it off, and do what we have said about reducing the fracture to treat a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it inclines to the side, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks appetite, and sweats, and perhaps vomits blood, and the movement of the bone ends can be felt clearly.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back, and a cushion is placed between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and align the ribs of both sides with your hands, carefully making it even in all ways possible until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply plasters and bandages made of thin salt cloth or other light fabric, wrap them around the splint on the broken bone so that they do not move; then tie a round bandage to the back tightly, and check each hour the bandaging, if it loosens, retighten it; and if it needs to be untied due to corrosion, itching, pain, or abscess, act quickly, untie it, remove the plaster, and address what has come about through various methods of treatment; then reapply the plaster and tie it tightly until it is secure.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of the ribs comes only in their thick part behind the back, and at the top because they are slippery; and one feels it well during examination with both hands.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedy is to place the fracture in an even position as is appropriate.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster, and bind it with a splint if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is inwardly displaced, the patient feels great pain and stabbing, as with pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; it leads to coughing up blood, vomiting large quantities of blood, and this is a serious illness, especially for the elderly.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to expel wind.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this so that low abscesses do not come if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, then heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say to apply suction cups to the area, to draw out forcefully, and this seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the cups will attract the excesses to the site due to the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say to cover the area with wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to evenly distribute the poultice, then treat it according to the treatment for pleurisy, with food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear due to a bone piercing the skin, and there is fear for the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the site of the broken rib, and place a tool underneath to protect the surface; and then one must cut the bone, and gently scrape, and then stitch together the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat with plasters until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses come, then place cloths moistened in rose oil on it; and treat the area as needed for an abscess, and have them lie awake on their side where it is necessary, until they are healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck (or collarbone)
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a fracture of the neck bones, and it can happen that they bend; and similarly with the spine.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be well or not, observe if you see his hands weakened, swollen, and dead-colored, and he cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many cases, and if they move and feel well when pinched and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and that the patient can be treated, if proper care is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens to the spine, and you want to know if they will be well or not, observe if the feet are weakened, and if there are symptoms like those in the hands, and on the back there is bloating and involuntary discharge; and when you lay them on their stomach, there is also involuntary discharge.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is laid on his back and wishes to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is deadly: do not labor in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not occur to him, then the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you should treat it if there is a hot abscess, applying spiny oil of roses or egg yolk oil until it is appeased; then apply one of the healing and drying plasters, and bind it with a cloth, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not let him sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone breaks, it must be cut above the chest; and remove the bone, then stitch together the two edges of the wound if it is large, using a suture, then treat with ointment that heals flesh until he is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the collar," place your left thumb there, making it equal to your right hand as best you can, then apply the plaster and bandage if needed; then bind it, and if there are any loose bones, cut them out, remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it does happen, there is only a slight shortening at the top; and it breaks lengthwise, and tilts inward, causing pain to the patient at the site, and bruising, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand over it, so that you are above the break; and feel where the fracture is and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the top, then make equal that fracture, so that it has a natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is lengthwise, where it tilts inward, then make the patient lie on their stomach, so that you can prepare for the restoration of that fracture.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, place the plaster on top, then put a splint of wood or horn, and hold the fracture still so that it does not move; and cover the area below the ribs, until the skin is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if hot abscesses occur, do not touch them until the hot abscess is calmed, and apply what we have said before; then return to restoration, and compress it as appropriate, if there are no adverse effects; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is what is between the neck and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then you must restore it according to one of the two methods: one of which is that you take a staff filled with healing ointment, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two heads with two ropes and pull them up, then seat the patient on a chair; then place the broken arm on the staff, up to the armpit, and have it curve around a wooden frame, then lift it with some heavy object or let the assistant hold it down; then set the fracture level with both hands, so that the bone returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you lift the patient onto his back, and tie the hand to his neck, then instruct two assistants that one pull what is above the fracture with both hands, and the other pull below at the joint, each stretching their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you wish that the extraction be stronger, then remove the ligament below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the tendons on its side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, then you must place one ligament below the collarbone, and another towards the side, below the fracture; and likewise if the fracture is towards the side, then you should place the ligaments gently, without labor, until the fracture is equal above and on the side; then set the fracture as it should be, and compress it, unless abscesses occur.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses occur, do not compress it for VII days, and place linen soaked in olive oil on it until the abscess is eased; then compress it, and the way to compress it is that you apply a poultice above the fracture, then bring the arm onto the shoulder, and place your hand either on the shoulder or breast; and cover with a cloth, and compress over the shoulder and arm so that the arm is in its natural position, unless something prevents it, or if the bone has moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and place over the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint one thumb’s width of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three thumbs’ widths on either side; then bind over the splints as I said at the beginning of the chapter over the fracture, more firmly and less in spreading.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the placement of the splints and the binding as we have said, when you restore the broken limb, and you fear a hot abscess, leave it bandaged until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine the bandages every three days to ensure that no itching or swelling occurs at the site where the new tissue cannot reach due to it being too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is reduced, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident occurs, do not dislocate it again for three days or more, and have the patient sleep on their back, with their hands on their stomach; place a cushion filled evenly with wool under the shoulder, and check every hour of day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move or soften the ligaments; reduce it by the power of medicine, and give them the food we mentioned before, in such a way that the food is initially soft; and when they begin to recover, let the food be more substantial.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset for forty days in total; then they must be dislocated and treated with baths and ointment medications to heal the area.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is tight and stuck, then wait one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
