Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "fascicles," of which one is small, and it is the one that is near the elbow; and the other is large, and it is the one below, toward the small wrist. Perhaps only the larger fascicle is broken, or perhaps the smaller one, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the smaller fascicle is broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing is quick; and when the larger one is broken, the healing is difficult, and more painful than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small phalanx that is merely broken, then it must be gently extended and placed evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large phalanx, then it must be more forcefully extended; and place him on a cushion, and elevate the pouched part of the hand higher than the others, and the small one lower than the other two, and let the patient lie crossed upon himself, with the cushion in front of him raised so that the patient feels no labor; then extend the minister's arm from below to his hand, or at the joint, and another minister above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the patient evenly, according to his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if there are multiple fractures, place each piece in its proper position, and if any are displaced causing pain to the heart, and you cannot restore it to its proper position, then cut it out as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the trepanning for wounds, I have spoken of it in a separate chapter; then take that treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the treatment abscesses appear, apply a strip of cerate made from rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard or too soft; and attach the strip gently, until the superficial abscesses are alleviated.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the cerate and apply the plaster made from powder of the mill with plenty of egg whites, then place the strips, and ensure that the strip over the trepanning should be slightly thicker and wider than the others; and note that it must have six strips on the arm in various positions: whether the trepanning is in one bone or two; and tighten more around the trepanning than elsewhere, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and ensure that the bandages over the trepanning are soft and moist, not hard or rough; and let the thread from which it is made be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And examine the limb and its joint after several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then it is necessary to rinse the limb with hot water until the itching subsides; and let the limb rest without pressure.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the compression, and if the joint is weakened and the bone dislocated, or similar things, address them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And be careful if the swelling cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you should loosen it a bit, and leave it like this for several days until the swelling can flow, and then compress it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to the patient, do not loosen them until twenty days have passed.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And when encircling it, then he can place his hands on his neck, and let his necks be equal, and beware of movement and shifting, and sleep lying on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and the natures of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and on both sides there are few fractures, and it rarely happens but many sprains occur.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or sprained, it is necessary that the patient sits with their crossed legs and sits straight in front of them evenly; then place his hand on an extended cloth, and let the healer extend the broken bones, and align them properly so they are well joined; and apply a plaster and bandages, unless abscesses occur, then put a splint according to the size of the area; and wrap it with one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the heel of the foot, make a pad of cloth, and instruct the patient to bind it to his fractured heel; and then bind with a long strip of cloth, and let the pad be as thick as the palm of the hand, and bind it, as is appropriate.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the side, then you must place one pad above and another below the sole of the foot, so that the hand is open and straight, then bandage it quickly around the hand, and secure the binding between the two pads.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture occurs on either of the two bones, and it is a comminuted fracture, place it evenly as appropriate; bind it with a pad, and if you wish, place a small straight pad to elevate the fracture, so that it does not move; and if the fracture is in one of the other bones, such as in the index finger or another, place it evenly, and bandage it with the healthy adjacent finger; or tie them all together as they should be moved, or place a pad under them like for a comminuted fracture; and take care during restoration and in the disposition of hot abscesses, and support those who come to you, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of a broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and this can be seen when it turns front and back; and the restoration is done by binding one bandage above the break and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their back, then each assistant extends their bandage equally on either side; this is when the break is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then one bandage should be towards the hip, and the other bandages below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the knee, then place one bandage near the knee, and extend it downwards; then set the bone equally between both hands so that it aligns naturally, and then apply a plaster, and bind it, unless abscesses interfere.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside then return to your work and treatment; the procedure is done in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should wrap the fracture with a bandage doubled over two or three times, and remove any excess; then turn the leg until the heels align at the base of the thigh, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg beside the knee, placing the ends of the thread above; then wind the bandage around the leg and thigh, then place splints on the fracture, and put one splint over the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and thigh with linen underneath to make the compression even, then begin to bind tightly three or four turns over the fracture; and as you move further from the fracture, reduce the tightness; then tie the two ends of the thread that you inserted between the leg and thigh, and tie three splints above them, then go back under the head of the thread until you reach near the foot; and bind it tightly so that it does not move from its place, then leave it as such, for no abscess or swelling will occur.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, dislocate it and address what comes next as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that cause pain, they must be removed if possible; and if not possible, the area should be cut open, and blood let; and treat it as we have said until he is well.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken in such a way that splints are applied, as with the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, in this kind of restoration, the patient does not suffer.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in 21 days, or a few less or more, according to the differences in temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee there is frequent bruising, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a crack, or an aperture, and it becomes like any wound, and feels as a wound, and this people feel well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that you put together those parts which are cut to their ends, as much as can be assembled; then apply the plaster, and if necessary place a round splint, and bind it as needed, then observe all the precautions we have mentioned for other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar cases; provide each case with what is appropriate until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by its proper name "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and it happens all sorts of breaks as they do to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is just as with the arm equally, and the work is done similarly. And if both bones are broken together, then turn the leg from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the finer bone is broken, then turn it forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the larger bone is broken, then there is great pain, and it can be seen clearly; and turn it backward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then treat with gentle extension, and set it evenly, and bind the splints equally; but nevertheless, if the break is severe and there are many pieces, the extension should be lighter and gentler; and handle it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of wood that will press the leg from one side and the other, and let them run along the length of the leg from the knee to below; then wrap it in two layers with a bandage above and below, and tie it securely in the middle as well, and at this point the leg cannot deviate to the right or left, and thus is well; some apply one plaster along the length of the leg, and if it's wood, they place the leg to prevent movement, and properly done is this in fractures where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess hot or another accident; treat it as long as necessary until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the foot bones
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but sometimes a fracture occurs in the bones of the foot and at the two joints, and it happens that it breaks in many conditions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bones of the foot and you see these bones overlap each other, place the patient's foot on the ground as if they were going to walk, then put your foot now on his where the bones are raised, then press them until they return to their places; then apply an emplastrum and bandages, and under the arch of the foot place a small board filled with two fists, then bind it tightly around the foot once you have wrapped cloths around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if one of the two is broken, then restore it as we have said about the two of the hand; then place a splint along the length of the bone, and make it slightly wider, then place under the foot the board I mentioned, and secure it tightly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place on each one a splint according to its size, wrapped in one piece of linen cloth, and secure the board under the foot; and let them be placed at the head of the board above the sole of the foot, so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have mentioned; and treat each case appropriately as is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's urethra is broken, make her sit expanded, then incline her towards the part of her back, and hold her from behind; then fill the woman's urethra with cotton, and place there as much wool as one holds in their fist; then stand the woman up and lift her back little by little, and then the cotton will come out until it reaches the entrance of the urethra, and return the bone with the wool; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and once she has urinated, put it back, and do this for seven days or around that time: the fracture will be restored, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, tie it to a tube, and pour all of the bladder into the urethra; then blow forcefully into the tube until the bladder is inflated inside: her urethra will return to its normal state; fill it with cotton again, and leave it like this for several days until she is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the thumb of a man is broken, or of a woman, restore it as we have said regarding the thigh bone; and these nearby fractures are not hidden from one who puts his study and use into them, and understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture indicates in many positions the proper way of restoration: understand then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the shaft, when it is broken, take a goose quill and insert the shaft into it; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three days or until healed, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, to be treated now, so that the treatments we have mentioned bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then staunch it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, and then restart the healing process at the same hour, or on that day, unless abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses come, then leave the restoration until a new day, until the abscesses are appeased, and do not touch them on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a harmful accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the exposed chest, then it must be set gently with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not available to set equal with your hands, then use this instrument made of iron, which is seven or eight inches long, and the width should be according to the size of the wound; and for this, it is necessary for the physician to take three or four, depending on what is needed for each treatment of fractures; let it be smooth and a little thick, so that it does not bend under compression on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp at the front, and thicker from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", for which the curved head should be placed on top of the visible bone; and push it in one go until it returns to being even with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone until the instrument can grip it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument, either an incisor or saw, to your ability; then remove what remains in the bone of hardness and small pieces.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you place it in its proper place, then moisten the joint with black styptic wine, and properly if it is in summer; and do not put cerate or anything else on the wound that has oil, for it will cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer bandages after you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not bound too tightly with the dressing; and many times foolish doctors have done this, and brought death or corrosion upon some patients; and let the bindings be looser than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that some evil may come of it as we have said, and you find pain in the area, then do not put bandages on it; but wrap around it, instead of bandages, hard cloths, and secure them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is producing pus, remove what you placed over it entirely, and put on healing salve, such as tetrahermion ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb should be positioned in such a way that the pus flows down gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and it cannot heal but continues to produce pus, know that there are small pieces of bone, so you must probe the wound with a probe, and remove all these loose pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or any other form of corruption, then it is necessary that you treat it, according to what he says in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar cases with large limbs, do not extract it, for many times death results from doing so; perhaps it will fall out by itself after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that come upon the joint
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see this after the injury, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a terrible sight to see the shape of the limb; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then when the body is cold: administer styptic medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others; so choose any of these things or all together, and mix them with styptic wine or with abundant egg white or with oil; and place it on the wound in bandages, and bind it tightly, and do not loosen it for several days; then remove it, and begin another one until the swelling is gone; or apply it to a well-made poultice; for the property of the poultice is that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, and needs to be removed, cut off the top, and reveal the excess apparent; or shave it with some shaver until it is gone, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb which is weak after recovery
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and the limb remains weak and delicate afterwards, it happens for many reasons: one being that it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been; or there were too many bindings, so nourishment could not reach the limb; or due to excessive washing; or because of too great movements, not at the proper time; or because they have little blood in their body, hence they are weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat and make the body soft, until the blood multiplies within him; then administer baths, give joy and rest; place pitch on the limb so that it attracts abundant nourishment, and wash frequently with cold water, until the nourishment reaches the limb; and thus restore its natural condition.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the limb twisted after the sickness
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone broken openly, and the form of the limb is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe those fools who say one must break the limb anew, and many foolish doctors have done this in our land; such work is condemned, and great harm comes from it, and perhaps death; yet if the ligaments and muscles are fresh, they should be bathed in hot water, or herbs that soften should be boiled, such as leaves of mallows, roots, and hellebore, and similar things; then make a softening ointment, such as well-made mithridate, and take the muscilaginous preparation of mallows, and mix it with fat from hen's flesh or oil of cumin, and apply an ointment on top; or take fatty figs, and grind them with linen flax, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the knot is removed to rub continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let movement be administered to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuousness is inflamed and hardened, like a stone, and needs to be removed with iron, then it must be cut up to the bone, carefully with a sharp knife; and apply cautery and care in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to anyone, it is necessary now to return it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the swelling increases, and by chance one may reset it to its place with difficulty; therefore, it is not right that one should move it while it is swollen: many times this brings on spasm and other pains. Nevertheless, when this happens, have the patient bled, then leave him until the swellings are appeased; then wash the limb with warm water and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each member as the cure may come in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It rarely happens that the mandibles are dislocated in both jaws, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: where they are a little out of their places, and softened a little; or where they are completely dislocated, and hang toward the side, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so it cannot be held, nor can it close its mouth, and envelops its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns on its own in many cases.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and accomplished, then you must reset it quickly and do not delay; and in such a way that the assistant holds the head of the patient, and places his fingers in the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides; and his other hand should be behind, to keep them even; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the doctor should place it evenly, so that it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to reset, especially if both jaws are involved, soak them in warm water and oil until you can gently reset them; do not delay in resetting them as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are reset evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well to soften it, place damp cloths made of rose oil and wax on them, then bind them gently with soft bandages; let the patient sleep on his back, and his head rest between two cushions so that he does not move left or right, nor strain to bite down, but eat light food until the pain subsides and the jaws are healed; and then eat lightly whatever he wants, without working to open the mouth for eating or drinking, until the jaw is well healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be reset perfectly in one hour, and are not returned to their places, it results in recurring fevers and habitual diarrhea, and possibly vomiting of bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then you know it is a prognosis of death; and many times the person who suffers from it dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	of strength
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The joint cannot be dislocated from the side within the continuation of the ribs and the hip, and it is sometimes dislocated outward, and this is well felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies supine on their back, and extends their arms; then press the area firmly with your palm, and it will return; then apply the plaster and bandage, and bind it tightly; and the head of the shoulder that is towards the side cannot be dislocated; if it can, and if it does dislocate at times, reset it to its place as we have said; then apply the plaster and bandage, and bind it tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until they are well; and similarly, the vertebrae of the spine that have been displaced from their place are returned in this manner.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated according to three manners: one of which is that it dislocates at the back part near the spine; and the second is at the lower part; and sometimes at the upper part, but this rarely happens; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor inside for the nerves; and more often it dislocates below towards the spine, especially in those who have little flesh, because it easily dislocates there; in those with enough flesh, it dislocates with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that there is a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they believe that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary then that you test it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	It is known that the dislocation occurs when it goes down towards the socket, and there is a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find their difference evident; and you will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and below the socket upon touching the head of the shoulder, as if it were an eye; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his face or move in any way; and similarly, if it is dislocated above, it is not hidden, for you find it evident by touch; and this kind of dislocation is not easily reducible when it is new, or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister lifts the patient's arm upwards, then places his fingers under the armpit, and raises the joint with force to its place; and the minister lifts the hand, and extends it upwards, then puts it down; it will quickly heal.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said within a few days, then the patient must be bathed in hot water; and the minister uses soothing and relaxing remedies, such as decoctions of elderflower, fenugreek, and honey-sweetened water; then the patient is rubbed on his back, and a piece of wool is placed under the armpit, neither too soft nor too hard, then place your foot under the armpit pad and raise the head of the shoulder forcefully, and pull the patient's hand; another minister holds the patient's head so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder will now return completely, and if you wish to reset it according to this method: have a man present who is taller than the patient; stand facing the side, put your shoulder under the armpit of the patient, lift the patient upwards, so that he hangs from your arm; another minister pulls the patient's hand downwards towards the abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he may hold something heavy with him, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is reset in another manner: take a long firebrand and place it in the ground such that the head of the shoulder aligns with it like an arrow; let it not be too thick nor too thin. Then place it under the patient but cover it with cloth, so the patient lies over the shaft; then extend their arm downwards on the other side, and the joint will quickly return to its place. And if it does not want to return despite all that we have said, do this cure: take a firebrand two arms' length long and four fingers wide, which has a sharp head to enter perfectly under the armpit, in this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie on the head of the barrel strips that do not hurt the patient, then place them under the seat of the patient; and extend his arm along the long barrel, and tie the shoulder to the barrel, and the arm at the top of the hand, then put the arm on one side of a broad ladder, and let the hands hang down, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will now gradually return.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, whatever the manner, you must put under the seat a sphere of even linen, then apply an ointment prepared with powdered miller's flour, with incense and egg albumen over the entire shoulder and around it, then stretch the patient gently from under the seat, and wrap the bandage over the ointment, and bind the hand to his neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eat little, until the limb is strengthened, because it will heal more quickly; and then eat more after 5 days or 7, and move it; and if it is firm and does not soften, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come into it, or for another reason, then you must administer cauterizations with three holes, as it is described before in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and after 7 days it loosens again, and the joint cannot be held, and he cannot raise his arm, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation towards the hip, and the breasts, or behind, is done by impulse, and extension of hands, and another minister attends to it; and care until he is well.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after recovery the member is stiff and slow in movement, the patient should take many baths until the stiffness is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the elbow
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the elbow is dislocated by points, and returns to them; and if it is dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not fixed, because it is seen clearly and felt distinctly; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick part with the healthy part, then you can see clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and he cannot bend his arm nor touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it as if abscesses were present, for if abscesses were to come, they would be difficult to remove; and perhaps it cannot be entirely reset, especially when it is at the back. It is worse than other dislocations, causes greater pain, and may result in death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such that when it can be reset, you should extend his hand with both your hands; and let his arm be spread out, and hold his hand around the joint, above and below, and bring the joint to its place at its base, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its proper position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strikes from the root of the palm the knife which is dislodged.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and when two ministers extend the arm, and the patient is held by two ministers, so that he cannot move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a double piece of cloth long and wide; and when the joints meet at his hand, apply some ointment to soften the joint, then forcibly insert the joint until it returns; and when it is in place, put on dry plaster with egg white, and tightly bind it to the neck of the patient, and leave it for several days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, undo the binding and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold tightly, redo the plaster and the bandage, and leave it like this for some days, until it is securely set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels stiffness after the joint is returned and it moves, bathe and rub gently, and press until it is relieved; or place on the joint a piece of fat lamb's wool, then leave it for one day and night, then remove it, and have him enter the bath; when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then put the wool back on, and then have him enter the bath again; do this two or three times until he is well; if you wish, place moistened oak leaves heated with butter over it; thus will he return to his condition.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is out of place, and its reduction is easy, more so than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place quickly, in the same hour that it is dislocated, before swelling occurs or an abscess develops.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the reduction is as follows: you place the affected hand on a table, and the assistant extends the hand. The therapist then places their palm over the appearance of the joint, pressing until it returns to its proper position. Nevertheless, you must check if it is in place; then have the patient place the back of their hand on a table during extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, have the patient place the back of their hand on a table, and the physician places their hand over that area of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is well. If not, apply emplasters to soothe the abscesses and leave it thus without repeating.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot place it back after several days, the joint remains dislocated. It does no harm to the patient as long as the limb is relaxed and cannot grasp anything: then you know that the nerves are severed or the artery; there is no other remedy but to cauterize near the case, and perhaps nothing else will help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when it is in place, apply the plaster we have mentioned, then press it and leave it for five days, then untie it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, then moisten it with warm water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the thumb of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the thumb of the hand is dislocated in any direction, either on the back or on the palm; then it must be placed straight, and the dislocation pushed back until it returns to place, then support the head of the thumb, and pull it towards the part where it is dislocated; and leave it for two days, then make it equal that day; and tie it as we have said, and untie it each day, and move it, and retie it at night; and do this often until it is tight, and also do this if it is dislocated on the palm of the hand, and do as you did before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated in another direction.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the backsplice
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the dislocation of the back or neck occurs, and there are many such dislocations, there is no remedy, for death swiftly overtakes the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that involuntary spasms occur, and they cannot be controlled, and sometimes certain limbs become weak, such as both legs or both arms or one. And often the dislocation moves to four parts; when it moves to the back, it is called "sciatica": the treatment is to determine if the sciatica has come from childhood: in that case, there is no cure or immediate healing.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And for those who come to it from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient methods of treatment were described with grand words, in which there is little benefit overall; but I have abbreviated them according to my understanding, and have fashioned instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the condition of clubfoot affecting the big toe, there is neither remedy nor cure; and likewise for those that affect directly two sides, which cannot be cured except properly as those affecting the back, as I said; and it should be that the patient lies stretched on his face in an even place, and has a pad beneath him so he does not hurt himself; then place one torch at the head in the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie a rope under the armpits of the patient, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two ministers hold the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two torches; and they should be well secured, the torch as we have said, and the physician places his palms on the spine firmly, until it relieves.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this cure, take a board three spans long and place it under the wall, and let the patient lie on his side, then put the end of the board under the wall, then place the middle of the board over the spine; and have the patient place his feet at the other end of the board, and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you wish, do this with a twist that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you fix two torches at the head of the patient from one arm's length apart, and near the feet two others, and there be between each torch, above and below, a palm’s space in length; and have in each torch one hole where the pulley can run, and let the torches be firmly fixed in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of two torches place one rotating torch upon which the ropes will turn, and at both rotating torches place two small torches of a palm's length for turning the pulleys; then tie the rope that is around the patient to the pulley towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other pulley, and each minister turns his own pulley along with all the ropes, and the master places the spine evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, place an absorbent plaster with plenty of egg, and then the cotton wool, and then a splinter from a board three fingers long, which covers the area of the curvature and the healthy part of the spine, then the sap of flax, as we have said, and the patient should use subtle nourishment until they are healed; and if anything comes at the end of healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the splinter that we mentioned above; and sometimes one administers a piece of lead, and sometimes an appearance occurs in the last vertebra of the back, and people think it is dislocation; but this bone appears because there should be no presumption about it: perhaps it would cause death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that at the joints of the hip and the shoulder, only dislocations occur, not like other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: inward and outward, and front and back; and more inward than elsewhere, and slightly dislocated in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the recognition of an inward dislocation is that when you join the affected leg with the healthy one, it appears longer, and the patient's knee is more bent than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee to the fire; and the area near it is swollen with abscesses and hot, because the thigh bone comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the signs of him who is coming to faint are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him who is about to be dislocated are that he extends his leg according to the completion; however, does not double the knee without pain, and if one wants to make him go, he cannot move forward, and retains his urine, and swells at the joint, and when he walks, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who is about to be dislocated behind are that he cannot extend his knee or bend it, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the joint is softened, and the head of the thigh is in a position below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment for this type of dislocation is to observe whether the dislocation is old, and if it persists according to its nature, there is no need for any intervention; it should not be attempted with presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and this is one of the four types of dislocations, hurry to return the joint, stretch it inwards and outwards, and move it from side to side; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare one strong assistant, and firmly grasp the leg with two hands, or tie it above the knee; another assistant places their hand above in such a way that they push their hands below the foot, then tighten them with a single bandage on the thigh; and another holds the head of the bandage; and pull upwards and downwards all at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to the four similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is correct.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then you must treat it accordingly When the dislocation is in the thigh joint, you should lift the patient onto their healthy side, then place the bandage at the root of the injured thigh, and below the groin; then stretch the bandage upwards towards the groin and towards the hip; take another assistant to hold the patient's arms, embrace the main part of the injured thigh, and extend it forcefully: it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot secure it in the manner we have described, then you must bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong bandage below the heels and above the knees; let the injured leg be extended two thumbs' width more than the other; then hang the patient by their head from a pole, and suspend them off the ground at arm's length; then instruct one assistant to embrace the upper part of the thigh, and have another assistant hanging with the patient who embraces forcefully the thigh, for now the joint will return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is out of place, the patient lies down, as we have said for him who has gout, and bind one cloth tightly on the affected leg, and similarly on the foot; then place two torches, one at the head and another at the feet, then insert a torch between the patient's thighs in the proper form; and place moist cloths around it so that it does not burn the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and the physician places his hand equally with the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
