Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on the table and press as we have said for gout, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when dislocation is before us, one must quickly stretch the diseased leg as I have said; and place the healer’s hand on top of the diseased joint, then press with the other hand, stretching it down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is towards the rear, one must not stretch the patient downward nor lift them up, but rather it should be as if the hip were dislocated to the side, as we have described for lying on both hips; and let him lie on his back, and extend the limb as we said before, and press on the joint with a board; and it is right when the patient extends their legs equally; then join the thighs together, apply the plaster, and bind them so that the hip does not move; and rest for three or four days, then unbind him, and put on the plaster again; and if you see that they are even, bind as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind, and make him walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: namely, inward and outward, and backward; it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not hold to his thigh, then you know it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such cases is as follows: you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your hands, then bend both sides of the knee forcefully; another assistant should extend his foot so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it holds well to his thigh lightly; then apply a plaster and bind the leg to the thigh tightly for three or four days, then release it; and do not allow the patient to walk until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not properly aligned, apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the thigh, until it is healthy
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes bruised, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inward and outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tight before the part where it is dislocated: the reduction is easy, and one should gently extend it with their hands when it is only bruised.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, you must have the patient sit upright, and hold the limb firmly just above the ankle; then pull the foot towards yourself with your right hand, and then twice with your left hand, then extend it upwards, and forcefully push the foot upwards; do this twice as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, continue the work, for it will return; and if it cannot return in this way, lie the patient on their back on the ground, and place a lever firmly in the ground between their thighs, and tie cloths around them so they do not move the patient; then hold one assistant by the thigh, and another assistant extend the foot with their hands or use a cord, tying it above the ankle joint; then both assistants should pull equally, and the lever should be steady between the patient's thighs to keep the patient still when extending; then place the doctors equally on the dislocation with their hands, and have one assistant hold the healthy leg behind, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is ready, place the plaster and plugs on, and wrap tightly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are behind the ankle, so the bandage is not too tight; then leave it for two days or three, and if the bandaging loosens, retighten it; then untie it on the third day or fourth, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if he walks before this term, it is no certainty that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if painful abscesses come, you must calm them as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both are dislocated, they must be gently extended without strain, and this is an easy task.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back of the foot, you must have the patient sit on a flat surface or on a table straight ahead, and place your foot over what appears to be his joints, then press firmly with your foot until it returns; and when they are even and there appears nothing amiss, put under the sole of the foot a board two fingers thick, then pull firmly, and leave for three days, then release him; and let him rest until he is well.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and of dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wishes to restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in the treatment if you are not wise in the art and have not practiced long, and if you are not compassionate and cautious rather than bold; and use soothing hot poultices at first, and leave the patient in God's hands if there is no hope of recovery; and when there is hope, now restore the limb to its place as hot poultices should come; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing hot poultices, and treat the wound as appropriate with drying ointments; and if along with dislocation there are fractures and small bones displaced, remove them, and do what we have said for simple diseases; and guard against entering a path of fear according to what I have said, for it is worth much more than your skill and strength.
Amen	So be it
